<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We had a <a href='../subjects/49' title='rain'>shower</a><span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. <a href='../subjects/9' title='Henry Anderson Brumfield'>Henry</a> and I got <span class='line-break'> </span> up with the <a href='../subjects/8059' title='turkeys'>turkeys</a>. <a href='../subjects/4' title='Benjamin Franklin Brumfield, Sr.'>Ben</a> &amp; <a href='../subjects/7353' title='Tim Bennett'>Tim</a> <span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/283' title='plowing'>plowed</a> some on the <a href='../subjects/258' title='corn'>corn</a> and<span class='line-break'> </span> helped <a href='../subjects/8169' title='Norman Booker'>Norman Booker</a> get up some<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/7301' title='hay'>hay</a>. Ben went to <a href='../subjects/7207' title='Gretna, Virginia'>Gretna</a> and<span class='line-break'> </span> got some <a href='../subjects/7523' title='flour'>flour</a> that <a href='../subjects/141' title='Jim Brumfield'>Jim</a> bought.<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/73' title='Hattie Gilbert'>Hattie</a> washed some this morning,<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/8086' title='Jennie Owen'>Mrs</a>. <a href='../subjects/7943' title='Mamie Hutcherson'>Mamie</a> <a href='../subjects/7323' title='Hutcherson'>Hutcherson</a> sent me<span class='line-break'> </span> some nice <a href='../subjects/236' title='cabbage'>cabbage</a> by Hattie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Booker sent me some <a href='../subjects/7277' title='green beans'>snaps</a><span class='line-break'> </span> by Jim. <a href='../subjects/8223' title='Miss Anna Hubbard'>Miss Anna Hubbard</a><span class='line-break'> </span> sent <a href='../subjects/8488' title='Josie'>Josie</a> some <a href='../subjects/390' title='bread'>light bread</a> by<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/7530' title='mail'>mail</a>. <a href='../subjects/7708' title='Mabel Brumfield'>Mabel</a> has cried a lot<span class='line-break'> </span> today. I hope she may feel<span class='line-break'> </span> better by morning. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> bought some <a href='../subjects/7574' title='beef'>beef</a> at Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked some of it for <a href='../subjects/71' title='supper'>supper</a>.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope to enjoy it.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2064">
<h3><a name="page-2064">Sunday, June 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We had a good <a href='../subjects/49' title='rain'>shower</a><span class='line-break'> </span> last night. We all staid at home<span class='line-break'> </span> all day except <a href='../subjects/9' title='Henry Anderson Brumfield'>Henry</a>. He went to<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/157' title='Johnson Reynolds'>Johnson Reynols</a> for a basket of <a href='../subjects/7314' title='peaches'>peches</a><span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/231' title='Earl Bennett'>Earl</a> &amp; <a href='../subjects/230' title='Lizzie Bennett'>Lizzie Bennett</a> come<span class='line-break'> </span> by to see <a href='../subjects/1627' title='Sally Joseph Carr Brumfield'>Josie</a> a while. <a href='../subjects/376' title='Posey Reynolds'>Posie<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols</a> &amp; <a href='../subjects/5' title='Marvin Smith'>Marvin Smith</a> com<span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes at night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> I got most of the <a href='../subjects/28' title='dinner'>dinner</a>.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cooked <a href='../subjects/236' title='cabbage'>cabbage</a> &amp; <a href='../subjects/239' title='potatoes'>potatoes</a><span class='line-break'> </span> and <a href='../subjects/7345' title='beets'>beets</a> &amp; <a href='../subjects/7574' title='beef'>beef</a>. We all enjoyed<span class='line-break'> </span> the beef. <a href='../subjects/32' title='Carrie Smith'>Carrie</a> &amp; the kids<span class='line-break'> </span> was at <a href='../subjects/138' title='Mollie Reynolds'>Mollies</a> to night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Wish I could see them.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Mollie &amp; Julia come from<span class='line-break'> </span> <a href='../subjects/7218' title='Norfolk, Virginia'>Norf.</a> today. I want to see them bad.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2065">
<h3><a name="page-2065">Monday, June 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and some rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Norman Booker was<span class='line-break'> </span> getting up wheat and had to stop.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben commenced to moow<span class='line-break'> </span> the hay and quit. Hattie<span class='line-break'> </span> Gilbert washed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The clothes is on the line<span class='line-break'> </span> now. Mollie Reynolds &amp; Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson come from Norfolk<span class='line-break'> </span> yesterday. Mollie was here<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that she come. Miss Sallie<span class='line-break'> </span> Trent got dinner today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was busy a bout other<span class='line-break'> </span> things. Mrs Car churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> That helper a lot. I do<span class='line-break'> </span> hope it will clear off to<span class='line-break'> </span> night. Hope everyone that wants<span class='line-break'> </span> to plant tobacco can do so.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2066">
<h3><a name="page-2066">Tuesday, June 20, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Rained a little. Jim &amp; Ben plowed<span class='line-break'> </span> in the corn. Henry plowed<span class='line-break'> </span> some two. Mrs. Car churned<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; strung snaps for dinner. Mrs.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mamie Hutcherson sent the<span class='line-break'> </span> snaps. Denias folks was looking<span class='line-break'> </span> for Henry &amp; his bride today.<span class='line-break'> </span> There has not bin any one<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie today. Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered a lot today, I am<span class='line-break'> </span> so sorry for her &amp; can't do<span class='line-break'> </span> any thing to help her.<span class='line-break'> </span> I started a letter to Effie<span class='line-break'> </span> today. Hope she may get<span class='line-break'> </span> it soon. Mrs. Trent helped<span class='line-break'> </span> me get dinner &amp; got supper.<span class='line-break'> </span> Had it about ready when<span class='line-break'> </span> I come home from milking.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2067">
<h3><a name="page-2067">Wednesday, June 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Ben &amp; Jim finished<span class='line-break'> </span> getting the wheat and cut<span class='line-break'> </span> the oats. They cut a few oats<span class='line-break'> </span> for Mr. Booker. Lizzie &amp; [Loney?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett come to see us today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad that they come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lenney carried all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> and I to [Renan?]. I went to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Kate a few minutes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Dr. Wigginton &amp; Pearl was<span class='line-break'> </span> there. I was glad to see them.<span class='line-break'> </span> The bees swarmed today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben hived them. I am getting<span class='line-break'> </span> vegetables a plenty now. The<span class='line-break'> </span> people around has bin very<span class='line-break'> </span> good to us. I know we are to<span class='line-break'> </span> be pittied. I am olde and<span class='line-break'> </span> give out &amp; Josie is sick and<span class='line-break'> </span> has to be waited on.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2068">
<h3><a name="page-2068">Thursday, June 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mr. Booker got up with hay<span class='line-break'> </span> all evening. Henry &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> plowed until noon. Mrs. Dews sent us some apples<span class='line-break'> </span> today Mrs. Trent [ironed?] all<span class='line-break'> </span> the morning. I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate come this evening and<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Josie some light<span class='line-break'> </span> bread. Johnson &amp; Mollie<span class='line-break'> </span> and Julie Fergerson<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. Mrs. Mamie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutchenson come and<span class='line-break'> </span> brought us some snaps.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am diapointed that<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie did not come to<span class='line-break'> </span> see me this evening.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2069">
<h3><a name="page-2069">Friday, June 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The men folks<span class='line-break'> </span> got up hay &amp; mowed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Edmons send us a bucket<span class='line-break'> </span> of snaps ready to put in the<span class='line-break'> </span> pot and a bag of apples.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Hutchenseon sent<span class='line-break'> </span> some light bread. [D__?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Blair come to see us to<span class='line-break'> </span> day. Mrs. Booker come. to day<span class='line-break'> </span> [Lula? Mayhen?] &amp; Elsie [Carter?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come and played with<span class='line-break'> </span> the children a while.<span class='line-break'> </span> The red cow have hurt<span class='line-break'> </span> her self so that she<span class='line-break'> </span> can't hardly get about.<span class='line-break'> </span> I want to see Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> so bad. I cant hardly stay at home<span class='line-break'> </span> and cant go<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2070">
<h3><a name="page-2070">Saturday, June 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Ben &amp; Jim &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker finished getting up the<span class='line-break'> </span> hay. Oscar [Brumfield?] &amp; Hugh<span class='line-break'> </span> and Grave and I went to White<span class='line-break'> </span> Falls. Grace and I fished. Oscar<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Hugh went to Mount [A__?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and played ball. Sallie<span class='line-break'> </span> come with Grace to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie. Mrs. [Doss?] come to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Josie today. Mollie came<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. I am glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> she come. When I got home<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Trent had milked<span class='line-break'> </span> the cows and had supper<span class='line-break'> </span> ready. I have bin looking<span class='line-break'> </span> for Carrie. I do hope<span class='line-break'> </span> they are well and and<span class='line-break'> </span> will come soon. I made all<span class='line-break'> </span> them marks while was sleeping.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2071">
<h3><a name="page-2071">Sunday, June 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We all staid at<span class='line-break'> </span> home. Mr. Trent &amp; I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. We cooked snaps &amp; [potatos?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and beets friend chickens<span class='line-break'> </span> made apple dumplings<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Anderson &amp; Denia Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie. Miss Janie<span class='line-break'> </span> and Anna Hubbard and<span class='line-break'> </span> Rob &amp; Ella and Mr. Sam<span class='line-break'> </span> all come to see Josie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Lewis sent her some<span class='line-break'> </span> nice peaches. Miss Anna<span class='line-break'> </span> brought her a box of<span class='line-break'> </span> tomatoes &amp; some light<span class='line-break'> </span> bread. Charley Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Carrie here a<span class='line-break'> </span> few minutes. I was so<span class='line-break'> </span> glad she come. I had<span class='line-break'> </span> thought of her all day.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2072">
<h3><a name="page-2072">Monday, June 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The boys finished<span class='line-break'> </span> getting up hay and oats and<span class='line-break'> </span> commence plowing tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Trent and I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie had bin feeling better<span class='line-break'> </span> today. Grace Brumsfield &amp; Lottie<span class='line-break'> </span> Kellie come to see Josie today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Grace brought some apples. Hattie Gilbert washed<span class='line-break'> </span> here today. I am glad to get<span class='line-break'> </span> her to wash. Henry got very<span class='line-break'> </span> mad today because we<span class='line-break'> </span> tied the dog. Mrs. [Eldens?] little<span class='line-break'> </span> baby was buried this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie B came this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> We are glad to have her.<span class='line-break'> </span> My cow is bad off in<span class='line-break'> </span> some way. I don't know<span class='line-break'> </span> what to do for her.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2073">
<h3><a name="page-2073">Tuesday, June 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning. Rained a<span class='line-break'> </span> shower at twelve oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span> It is raining tonight. The<span class='line-break'> </span> men plowed in the tobacco all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Isla Blair come today and<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Josie some light bread.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr. and Mrs. [Tower?] &amp; [Edieth?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come. Mrs. Owen come and Mr.<span class='line-break'> </span> [Jennings?] the preacher come.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey &amp; [Carrie?] and Reese<span class='line-break'> </span> the other children was at<span class='line-break'> </span> [?] Brumfields. We<span class='line-break'> </span> gathered some peaches and<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. [?] made preserves'of them. I heard today<span class='line-break'> </span> that my brother is sick.<span class='line-break'> </span> I do hope he may get well.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so anxious to hear a<span class='line-break'> </span> gain.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2074">
<h3><a name="page-2074">Wednesday, June 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We had a good rain<span class='line-break'> </span> last night. Jim and Ben and Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> pulled the weeds from among <span class='line-break'> </span> peas. They helped Norman<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker load on some logs<span class='line-break'> </span> to carrie to the Saw Mill.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> his can to Gretna. She was<span class='line-break'> </span> going to Lynchburg. I went<span class='line-break'> </span> with them. We brought bread<span class='line-break'> </span> and ship stuff and sugar meal. We<span class='line-break'> </span> had a good trip. Nellie and<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Trent had the work<span class='line-break'> </span> done. Mrs Trent milked for<span class='line-break'> </span> one. I am glad of their being<span class='line-break'> </span> so good to me. Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> sit on the porch [some?]<span class='line-break'> </span> today.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2075">

Ben &amp; Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> helped thrash wheat at<span class='line-break'> </span> Johnson [Reynolds?]. Mollie came<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie this evening. [Kate?]<span class='line-break'> </span> HUbbard for her in the car.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker come for a whil<span class='line-break'> </span> [Nellie?] sent [?] a<span class='line-break'> </span> dress today. Janie [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come ion a few minutes<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. Heard from my brother<span class='line-break'> </span> They though he was [some?]<span class='line-break'> </span> better. I hope he may get well.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-2076">

Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> has had a bad day. <div id="page-2081">
<h3><a name="page-2081">Wednesday, July  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The land is [two?]<span class='line-break'> </span> wet to work. Jim &amp; Ben [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco most of the day. They<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Norman Booker fix<span class='line-break'> </span> a [top?] for his well this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. Mrs. Trent &amp; Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> [caned?] sixteen quarts of<span class='line-break'> </span> apples this morning. Effie<span class='line-break'> </span> went to [Reynolds?] and<span class='line-break'> </span> spent the day. Mrs. Tren<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Nellie went this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> [Robbert?] brought them<span class='line-break'> </span> home on the car. I have bin [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> all day. We got [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> first cabbage to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Snaps has [grown?]</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2082">
<h3><a name="page-2082">Thursday, July  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. The men [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco. Miss Sally [?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie picked and caned some<span class='line-break'> </span> berries. I got dinner. Mrs. [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> was sick. She is better tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening [?] Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Aunt Effie. [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Kate come to see Josie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Bates &amp; Mrs. White &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> three children come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Effie. Got a [phone?] message<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening that my brother<span class='line-break'> </span> Letcher dies this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> at 8 oclock. I am very<span class='line-break'> </span> sorry to hear of his [deth?]<span class='line-break'> </span> He will be missed by his<span class='line-break'> </span> children. I want to go<span class='line-break'> </span> to the burial if any one<span class='line-break'> </span> will take me.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2083">
<h3><a name="page-2083">Friday, July  7, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day today. Jim [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> has bin sick all day. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> helped Booker thrash wheat this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. Johnson [Reynolds?] went<span class='line-break'> </span> to [?] to day Mollie and <span class='line-break'> </span> [?] and I went with<span class='line-break'> </span> him. Went to [Lethcer's?] house<span class='line-break'> </span> but did not go to the graveyard.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children seemed badly<span class='line-break'> </span> hurt. I know they will<span class='line-break'> </span> miss him so much. I saw a <span class='line-break'> </span> lot of folks that I know<span class='line-break'> </span> and a lot of kind folks.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie &amp; Mrs. [Car?} and Mrs. Trent<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner &amp; staid with<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie. [?] [Bennett?] come for<span class='line-break'> </span> Effie late this evening. Hattie<span class='line-break'> </span> washed here this morning.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2084">
<h3><a name="page-2084">Saturday, July  8, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Clouds this evening <span class='line-break'> </span> but no rain to do any good. <span class='line-break'> </span> They thrashed wheat here this <span class='line-break'> </span> morning. Made 99 Bushels. We <span class='line-break'> </span> did not feed any body. The boys <span class='line-break'> </span> plowed [thene?] tobacco this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs. Car and Mrs. Trent went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Cedar Forest Church to<span class='line-break'> </span> day. Nellie wored on Mrs. <span class='line-break'> </span> Trents dress. I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie washed dishes after<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. Nellie baked a<span class='line-break'> </span> cake this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> I killed and dressed <span class='line-break'> </span> two chickens for dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> to morrow. I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> when Mrs. Car and Mrs. Trent<span class='line-break'> </span> got home I was so afraid that<span class='line-break'> </span> they would get wet.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2085">
<h3><a name="page-2085">Sunday, July  9, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. We all staid at home all the morning. Mrs. Trent and I got dinner. This evening Ben carried Nellie to [gretna?]. Jim and I went with him. We all went to [Marvins?] They were all well. [Reese?] carried aunt Nell to the station. The we started home. Oscar Brumfield had trouble with his car. Ben helped him get it to run a gain it made us late. Mr. Hubbard and Family and Ellen and two of her children cam to see Josie. I am glad that they came. Would of liked to see them myself. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2086">
<h3><a name="page-2086">Monday, July 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim plowed in <span class='line-break'> </span> the [Toleaces?] Ben Helped<span class='line-break'> </span> thrash wheat at Ann [Edmons?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and at Mayhews.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got Dinner.  Mrs [Trent?]<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed.  We had no company<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I went to Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Bookers to see Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Ronner an olde Lady.  She<span class='line-break'> </span> is Mrs Bookers grandmother.<span class='line-break'> </span> Denis &amp; [Coralie?] was at<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Bookers but did not<span class='line-break'> </span> stay long they thought<span class='line-break'> </span> it was going to rain but<span class='line-break'> </span> it did not.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2087">
<h3><a name="page-2087">Tuesday, July 11, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very hot day.<span class='line-break'> </span> A good day.  The boys finished <span class='line-break'> </span> plowing corn &amp; tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Then commence to plowing <span class='line-break'> </span> peas. Josie got a letter <span class='line-break'> </span> from Effie Brumfield &amp; Thelma<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Marys pictures.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Trent ironed all the<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Mrs Car churned<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; strung the snaps for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  I set<span class='line-break'> </span> a round most of the<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Mrs Trent sewd<span class='line-break'> </span> some. I wanted to go<span class='line-break'> </span> some where that I could<span class='line-break'> </span> fish but could not go.<span class='line-break'> </span> I miss Reese so much.<span class='line-break'> </span> Some of them here has me<span class='line-break'> </span> where they want me - work<span class='line-break'> </span> and stay at home.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2088">
<h3><a name="page-2088">Wednesday, July 12, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day - very warm.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim finished plowing<span class='line-break'> </span> the peas.  Ben went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Bailisses.  There was<span class='line-break'> </span> a picknick at [Gladys?] to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  There was lots of people<span class='line-break'> </span> there so them that was there<span class='line-break'> </span> say.  Hugh Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> carried Henry and I to the<span class='line-break'> </span> mill at Whitefalls.  We did<span class='line-break'> </span> not catch many fish [mollies?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynolds &amp;  [Johnson?] come to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie Gilbert washed<span class='line-break'> </span> here to day.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2089">
<h3><a name="page-2089">Thursday, July 13, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. rain tonight we are <span class='line-break'> </span> glad of it. Jim and Ben Topped <span class='line-break'> </span> Tobacco all morning They dug <span class='line-break'> </span> Potatoes this evening and <span class='line-break'> </span> sowed some peas. Josie has <span class='line-break'> </span> tried to work some today with <span class='line-break'> </span> her punch needle. Mrs. Trent <span class='line-break'> </span> ironed all the morning. Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> shelled butter beans the first that <span class='line-break'> </span> we have had. We had tomatoes <span class='line-break'> </span> for the first [time] this year.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> I got dinner cooked cabbage <span class='line-break'> </span> and butter beans &amp; baked <span class='line-break'> </span> apples. This evening I <span class='line-break'> </span> hemed a table cloth. Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> helped me milk what she <span class='line-break'> </span> could. We have not had <span class='line-break'> </span> any company today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Well I am most a sleep. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2090">
<h3><a name="page-2090">Friday, July 14, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning clear this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Ben helped to raise<span class='line-break'> </span> a barn at Dick Woodings. Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Reynols and got a big<span class='line-break'> </span> basket full of nice peaches.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Trent and Mrs Car and I peeled <span class='line-break'> </span> them.  We had peaches and cream <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner and supper and Mrs Car <span class='line-break'> </span> caned 13 quarts.  I am so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> of them.  Mrs Trent ironed to<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  I hemed a table cloth.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner cooked snaps<span class='line-break'> </span> and cymblings and fried two<span class='line-break'> </span> chickens.  I went to the orchard<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening and got a few<span class='line-break'> </span> apples and a few peaches.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> glad of the fruit this time.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie is suffering to night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2091">
<h3><a name="page-2091">Saturday, July 15, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys topped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all morning.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Chatham this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried him to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> I went as far as Coleman <span class='line-break'> </span> Mayhews.  Mathew Mayhew <span class='line-break'> </span> buried this evening. Mr Barber<span class='line-break'> </span> preached his funeral.  There was <span class='line-break'> </span> a big crowd at the burial.<span class='line-break'> </span> I did not go to the grave.  Carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> and Marvin and four of the <span class='line-break'> </span> children come and I come with<span class='line-break'> </span> them home.  They eat supper <span class='line-break'> </span> with us.  Mrs Trent went<span class='line-break'> </span> home this evening.  I was very <span class='line-break'> </span> sorry to see her go.  Grace <span class='line-break'> </span> sent me some apples<span class='line-break'> </span> by Ben.  I was glad of them.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2092">
<h3><a name="page-2092">Sunday, July 16, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Mrs Car &amp; Henry made<span class='line-break'> </span> ice cream.  I got dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> fried chicken cooked <span class='line-break'> </span> butter beans &amp; potatoes<span class='line-break'> </span> baked tea cakes. Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> looked for Jims turkey <span class='line-break'> </span> did not find her.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim come home with <span class='line-break'> </span> Norman Booker from <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna. Jo Edmons and [Jac?son]<span class='line-break'> </span> Emerson come to see Henry.<span class='line-break'> </span> They all went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> branch to bathe.  Josey<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Johnson &amp; Charlott come<span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes.  Edna helped <span class='line-break'> </span> milk this morning &amp; tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Oh Lord take care of all of us.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2093">
<h3><a name="page-2093">Monday, July 17, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Clouds about<span class='line-break'> </span> but did not rain here.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben &amp; Henry[?] suckered tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  Marvin &amp; Rose<span class='line-break'> </span> Smith eat dinner with us.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad to have them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker came to see <span class='line-break'> </span> us this evening.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> churned and helped shell <span class='line-break'> </span> butter beans &amp; scraped <span class='line-break'> </span> potatoes helped me get <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner what she could.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got cabbage &amp; cymblings <span class='line-break'> </span> and butter beans cucumber <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; tomatoes &amp; potatoes for <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Hattie [Gillient?]<span class='line-break'> </span> washed here today.  Kate Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> come this morning. </div>

<div id="page-2094">
<h3><a name="page-2094">Tuesday, July 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning rain this eve <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; tonight.  The boys suckered <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco this morning.  Ben [drawed?]<span class='line-break'> </span> the wheat out of the box. It <span class='line-break'> </span> was heating.  He intended going <span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill if it had not<span class='line-break'> </span> rained.  Ben &amp; Henry went <span class='line-break'> </span> to the store tonight.  Have <span class='line-break'> </span> got in at nine o'clock.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car churned and shelled <span class='line-break'> </span> butter beans and scraped<span class='line-break'> </span> potatoes.  We get plenty <span class='line-break'> </span> tomatoes now.  Ella Hubbard<span class='line-break'> </span> sent Josie a nice basket of<span class='line-break'> </span> tomatoes by Nat Wooding<span class='line-break'> </span> today. I got a letter from <span class='line-break'> </span> Effie Brumfield today was <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to get it am always <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to hear from them</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2095">
<h3><a name="page-2095">Wednesday, July 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Jim went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Ned Walkers to help him<span class='line-break'> </span> cover a house.  Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> the mill did not get all <span class='line-break'> </span> of his grinding done.  He <span class='line-break'> </span> topped tobacco this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> The Moorfields come for <span class='line-break'> </span> Rock a bout their flues.<span class='line-break'> </span> Max Car come late this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening. Carrie sent a<span class='line-break'> </span> box of something to eat to<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  She sent it to Renon.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went after it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Baker sent some <span class='line-break'> </span> light bred by Ray.  It was<span class='line-break'> </span> nice.  Josie eat some of it<span class='line-break'> </span> while it was warm.  I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner and ironed some this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Josie is suffering so bad.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2096">
<h3><a name="page-2096">Thursday, July 20, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The men suckered<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  Max Car<span class='line-break'> </span> went from here this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Denia Blair come to see <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie this evening.  She brought<span class='line-break'> </span> some nice strawberries<span class='line-break'> </span> that Sallie Blair sent to <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  Nat Wooding sent <span class='line-break'> </span> her 4 peaches very nice.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynolds come to <span class='line-break'> </span> see Josie late this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Car helped me what <span class='line-break'> </span> she could.I starched <span class='line-break'> </span> the clothes. Intend to iron<span class='line-break'> </span> in the morning.  Several of<span class='line-break'> </span> the people met at Straight<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone this evening and cleaned<span class='line-break'> </span> up the church.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2097">
<h3><a name="page-2097">Friday, July 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim &amp; N<span class='line-break'> </span> worked in the tobacco part<span class='line-break'> </span> of the day.  Lizzie and [Louisa?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett and my sister Mrs [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come today.  I was so glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> they come.  Mrs Edmons &amp; Jamie<span class='line-break'> </span> Gravely come to see Josie a little <span class='line-break'> </span> while.  Mrs Hutcherson come<span class='line-break'> </span> and Julia Fergerson &amp; Reubin<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols come a little while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Edmons brought apples,<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Hutcherson apples &amp; peaches<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; plums, Lizzie brough a cake<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; ban[a]nas.  I am glad of all <span class='line-break'> </span> the kindness that is bestowed<span class='line-break'> </span> on Josie.  Little Paul Smith<span class='line-break'> </span> eat dinner with us.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went home this evening.</p>

<div id="page-2098">
<h3><a name="page-2098">Saturday, July 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Ben &amp; Henry went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Marvin Smiths to hunt<span class='line-break'> </span> minks.  Could not start any.<span class='line-break'> </span> They eat breakfast up there.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben looked for <span class='line-break'> </span> the turkeys that is missing<span class='line-break'> </span> but did not find them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Grace B come and brought<span class='line-break'> </span> us some apples. Lee come<span class='line-break'> </span> and got the cider mill.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to spend the <span class='line-break'> </span> night with Hugh Brumfield. <span class='line-break'> </span> I have not worked much<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Would be glad I had <span class='line-break'> </span> done more.  Will have to <span class='line-break'> </span> make up for my idleness<span class='line-break'> </span> to morrow if I am able.<span class='line-break'> </span> I heard today that Levi East is<span class='line-break'> </span> dead.  I knowed him when he was a little boy. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2099">
<h3><a name="page-2099">Sunday, July 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  We all staid at<span class='line-break'> </span> home all the morning then<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; the children and Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Car went to Jim [Powers?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Alice Thomson and Kate <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard &amp; Christenia Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> come.  Alice brought Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> a box of figs.  Christenia <span class='line-break'> </span> brought some [ice?].  Carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; her children come.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> was with them and went<span class='line-break'> </span> back with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has not suffered so<span class='line-break'> </span> much to day.  I hope<span class='line-break'> </span> she may sleep tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie brought Josie  a <span class='line-break'> </span> box of grapes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2100">
<h3><a name="page-2100">Monday, July 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna to meet Jim &amp; Nel.<span class='line-break'> </span> They come got here for <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. This evening Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went to White Falls<span class='line-break'> </span> for flour.  All the children <span class='line-break'> </span> and I went &amp; fished.<span class='line-break'> </span> Some caught several small<span class='line-break'> </span> fish one eel did not bring <span class='line-break'> </span> them home.  Ben had all <span class='line-break'> </span> he could manage on his <span class='line-break'> </span> car.  We come by <span class='line-break'> </span> Renons.  Ben bought some <span class='line-break'> </span> things.  I think most <span class='line-break'> </span> every body is getting ready<span class='line-break'> </span> for the meeting.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so near asleep<span class='line-break'> </span> that I keep scratching <span class='line-break'> </span> up my book.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2101">
<h3><a name="page-2101">Tuesday, July 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning rain late<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  The men worked <span class='line-break'> </span> in the tobacco all day.  Lizzie<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett was with us today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alma &amp; Louise went to [st..?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone to the assosiation.  We are<span class='line-break'> </span> very glad to have Lizzie with us.  <span class='line-break'> </span> We have not fixed any<span class='line-break'> </span> thing on account of sickness.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Hutcherson and Ada come<span class='line-break'> </span> by this evening and brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie a nice box of things to <span class='line-break'> </span> eat.  We have a lot of<span class='line-break'> </span> vegetables now.  We heard<span class='line-break'> </span> that Carrie was at the <span class='line-break'> </span> meeting.  I would of liked<span class='line-break'> </span> to see all the folks that<span class='line-break'> </span> I know that was there.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2102">
<h3><a name="page-2102">Wednesday, July 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day but no rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> The men worked in the <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Strait Stone to<span class='line-break'> </span> the meeting.  I think he had<span class='line-break'> </span>  a fine time.  Mrs [Dews?] &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Power come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  Farmor Dews brought<span class='line-break'> </span> them.  They brought Josie a <span class='line-break'> </span> box.  Mrs Kellie sent her<span class='line-break'> </span> a box. Mr Thomson sent<span class='line-break'> </span> her some ice.  Nellie cand[sic]<span class='line-break'> </span> five cans of tomatoes.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> churned.  Jim &amp; Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> killed the bees tonight.  <span class='line-break'> </span> That is the last of<span class='line-break'> </span> my having any thing<span class='line-break'> </span> to do with bees I guess.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2103">
<h3><a name="page-2103">Thursday, July 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim went to Ned Walkers<span class='line-break'> </span> and helped to cover<span class='line-break'> </span> a stable.  Henry worked <span class='line-break'> </span> in the tobacco.  I cut the<span class='line-break'> </span> honey out of [qu..?]. Nella[?]<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  Mrs Edmons<span class='line-break'> </span> sent some cake and chicken<span class='line-break'> </span> her this morning.  Lillian <span class='line-break'> </span> Kent come up here this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  She brought cake<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; some nice meat. Every<span class='line-break'> </span> one has bin so good to<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  Mrs Car is very<span class='line-break'> </span> sick.  The Doc was to <span class='line-break'> </span> see her this evening.  Kate<span class='line-break'> </span> come and staid with us<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.  Ben has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> after Ella Hubbard [near?] 9 o'clock.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2104">
<h3><a name="page-2104">Friday, July 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  A thunder-cloud<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight not much rain yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> The men worked in the tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to [Strait?] Stone<span class='line-break'> </span> at twelve o'clock for ice.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has not suffered<span class='line-break'> </span> so much to day.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> has bin very sick all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Dews come by this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  He brought plums<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; pears and apples.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> glad of the apples.  Lawson<span class='line-break'> </span> Power come by to see<span class='line-break'> </span> his Grandma &amp; Josie.  He was<span class='line-break'> </span> on his way to Mr [Farrows?].<span class='line-break'> </span> They are having a [crowd?]<span class='line-break'> </span> there tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate [Hanerey?]staid with Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Car last night.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2105">
<h3><a name="page-2105">Saturday, July 29, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry worked on the tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> all the morning. This evening <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried me &amp; all the <span class='line-break'> </span> children to Cedar Forest.<span class='line-break'> </span> I fished some.  Caught <span class='line-break'> </span> three fish. Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Powers. We come by <span class='line-break'> </span> Thomsons Store.  We bought <span class='line-break'> </span> a few things some cups &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> sausers[sic].  Nellie &amp; Ella<span class='line-break'> </span> peeled some peaches &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie caned[sic] them and<span class='line-break'> </span> some tomatoes.  Josie went <span class='line-break'> </span> up stairs and staid with<span class='line-break'> </span> her mother some today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car has bin in bed<span class='line-break'> </span> two day[s].  Mollie Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see the sick.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2106">
<h3><a name="page-2106">Sunday, July 30, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day rain tonight.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Norman Booker walked <span class='line-break'> </span> around in the crop all the <span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Ben carried Ella<span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard home.  All the<span class='line-break'> </span> children went with him.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie and I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Louisa John &amp; family<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  The Boys got <span class='line-break'> </span> their first water<span class='line-break'> </span> mellons[sic] today.  I peeled <span class='line-break'> </span> 4 pounds of pears today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Gathered some snaps <span class='line-break'> </span> for tomorrows dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car come to <span class='line-break'> </span> the table to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so glad she <span class='line-break'> </span> is better.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2107">
<h3><a name="page-2107">Monday, July 31, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on their tobacco all day.  Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> has bin very busy today.  she <span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner &amp; churned gathered <span class='line-break'> </span> some grapes to make jellie.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Miss Willie<span class='line-break'> </span> Woodings burial. There was<span class='line-break'> </span> a big crowd at the burial.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went with Mr Booer[sic] &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> family. It was kind of <span class='line-break'> </span> him to take me.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> has him up all day or nearly<span class='line-break'> </span> so.  This evening I cut some<span class='line-break'> </span> grass in the garden and<span class='line-break'> </span> gathered a few snaps <span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner tomorrow.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie washed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children and I got the<span class='line-break'> </span> clothes in tonight.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2108">
<h3><a name="page-2108">Tuesday, August  1, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Henry worked<span class='line-break'> </span> in the tobacco.  Ben went to<span class='line-break'> </span> [Renan?].  He was one of the judge[s] of the <span class='line-break'> </span> election.  [Irvin? or John?] Harvey come for<span class='line-break'> </span> me &amp; brought me home.  The<span class='line-break'> </span> children went with me. <span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Kate Harveys &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> staid a little while.  Jamie <span class='line-break'> </span> Gravely was there.  Virginia &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Jamie was fixing up their supper<span class='line-break'> </span> to take on a hay ride.  They <span class='line-break'> </span> have a beautiful night for their<span class='line-break'> </span> ride.  Nellie made some jellie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; caned[sic] tomatoes this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car strung the snaps<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; shelled butter beans &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> churned.  I gathered <span class='line-break'> </span> tomatoes and corn.  I cooked <span class='line-break'> </span> it all.  We had two [water?] mellons. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2109">
<h3><a name="page-2109">Wednesday, August  2, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys helped<span class='line-break'> </span> cut tobacco at Norman<span class='line-break'> </span> Bookers.  Jim &amp; Henry eat<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner at Bookers.  Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> come home.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Pearl Wiggonton &amp; and her <span class='line-break'> </span> mother &amp; Virginia Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Alice Carter come a few <span class='line-break'> </span> minutes.  Mrs Booke[r] come.<span class='line-break'> </span> She brought some snaps.<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; peas.  Kate brought snaps.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad of them.<span class='line-break'> </span> We have had two fine <span class='line-break'> </span> musk mellons today.  Max<span class='line-break'> </span> Car come this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so near asleep<span class='line-break'> </span> that I cant write.</p>
</div>

<br />
<div id="page-2110">
<h3><a name="page-2110">Thursday, August  3, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The men worked <span class='line-break'> </span> in their tobacco most of the <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Late this evening Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr Dews for<span class='line-break'> </span> fruit.  the children and <span class='line-break'> </span> I went with him.  He got <span class='line-break'> </span> pears &amp; apples and plums <span class='line-break'> </span> and some snaps. We come <span class='line-break'> </span> by the Store and got sugar.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie made some jellie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; caned some tomatoes.  I<span class='line-break'> </span> got most of the dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car is here yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has not felt so good<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  There has not bin any<span class='line-break'> </span> one to see her to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I milked when I got back<span class='line-break'> </span> from Dews as it was about<span class='line-break'> </span> dark.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2111">
<h3><a name="page-2111">Friday, August  4, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  the boys shod<span class='line-break'> </span> horses 7 plowed a little in <span class='line-break'> </span> the garden.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried Jim &amp; Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna.  Nellie would<span class='line-break'> </span> go home and Jim went <span class='line-break'> </span> with her.  Mrs Anderson<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Fannie Hendricks come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie and the children <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  I was so glad <span class='line-break'> </span> that they come.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> and Nellie &amp; Josie peeled <span class='line-break'> </span> a lot of little pears today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I intend pickling and<span class='line-break'> </span> preserving them in the morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I will miss Nellie tomorrow.<span class='line-break'> </span> Will make out some way.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2112">
<h3><a name="page-2112">Saturday, August  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day until near night then <span class='line-break'> </span> a rain &amp; wind and some<span class='line-break'> </span> hail.  I hope not enough to<span class='line-break'> </span> damage any thing much.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry cleared up <span class='line-break'> </span> a barn getting ready to <span class='line-break'> </span> cut tobacco.  Ben has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to Bookers barn now.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car bathed the <span class='line-break'> </span> children this evening.  Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Dews sent me some snaps<span class='line-break'> </span> by Mr Nat Wooding.  I am <span class='line-break'> </span> glad of them. I made one<span class='line-break'> </span> jar of preserves &amp; one of <span class='line-break'> </span> pickle, and near a gallon<span class='line-break'> </span> of jellie made the <span class='line-break'> </span> damsons that Carrie brought<span class='line-break'> </span> all in jellie.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2113">
<h3><a name="page-2113">Sunday, August  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> The cows got in the corn.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry got them out.<span class='line-break'> </span> Posie &amp; Julia come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  they had Mildred &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Charlott with them.  The Reynols <span class='line-break'> </span> got home from their trip<span class='line-break'> </span> to Baltimore late yesterday.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad they are at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Acie Anderson brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie &amp; Edith Power to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had colde supper<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Mrs Car washed<span class='line-break'> </span> the dishes then Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Marvin come.  I had enough <span class='line-break'> </span> for them.</p>

<div id="page-2114">

Mrs Car peeled <span class='line-break'> </span> and caned five cans of<span class='line-break'> </span> tomatoes this morning,  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I went with<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna to Reynols.  Julia <span class='line-break'> </span> wanted to fit her dresses.<span class='line-break'> </span> She staid until supper.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went after her &amp; went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> Store.  Henry &amp; Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span> every body is so [leryst?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker sent me some<span class='line-break'> </span> snap for tomorrows dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry &amp; Franklin went <span class='line-break'> </span> with Ben to the Store <span class='line-break'> </span> to night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2115">
<h3><a name="page-2115">Tuesday, August  8, 1922</a></h3>

Mollie <span class='line-break'> </span> gave them to me. Kate<span class='line-break'> </span> Harvey come a while [yes?]<span class='line-break'> </span> I keep busy all the time<span class='line-break'> </span> when I will.</p>

<div id="page-2116">

Josie has not felt <span class='line-break'> </span> as well as usual today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna &amp; Franklin went<span class='line-break'> </span> to the Store this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> for medicine. I got some<span class='line-break'> </span> snaps from our cornfield<span class='line-break'> </span> the first [....?]<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2117">
<h3><a name="page-2117">Thursday, August 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Marvin carried me to <span class='line-break'> </span> Galilee to the assosiation.<span class='line-break'> </span> After preaching Lizzie &amp; Lonny[?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and Earl and wife Marvin<span class='line-break'> </span> and Carrie &amp; the children and I<span class='line-break'> </span> went to the place we moved <span class='line-break'> </span> from. <div id="page-2118">

<div id="page-2119">
