<p> Ben cut Edna's hair<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. He certainly<span class='line-break'> </span> did hate to do it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna helped me milk to night. <span class='line-break'> </span>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2142">
<h3><a name="page-2142">Monday, September  4, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day rain tonight<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Emerson and little <span class='line-break'> </span> daughter come in here<span class='line-break'> </span> out of the cloud. She had <span class='line-break'> </span> bin to Renan <span class='line-break'> </span> to meet her mother.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim quit his [house?] of  <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Two colered girls picked<span class='line-break'> </span> the dried beans today.<span class='line-break'> </span> We looked for Lizzie <span class='line-break'> </span> Bennett this evening.  She <span class='line-break'> </span> did not come.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Ben tried to start<span class='line-break'> </span> his engine today.  It <span class='line-break'> </span> would not start. <span class='line-break'> </span> We all are sorry a bout it.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2143">
<h3><a name="page-2143">Tuesday, September  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Mrs Emerson <span class='line-break'> </span> went from here by the <span class='line-break'> </span> time she could see to travel. <span class='line-break'> </span> I hope she got home OK.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and the children<span class='line-break'> </span> picked up some apples <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Ben carried Mrs Car to <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim Powers this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> I went as far as Cedar<span class='line-break'> </span> Forest.  I fished some.  Did <span class='line-break'> </span> not catch any thing any [.....?].<span class='line-break'> </span> I walked most all the way <span class='line-break'> </span> from Cedar Forest to Mr Powers<span class='line-break'> </span> before I met Ben.  We got <span class='line-break'> </span> home in good time.  Nellie milked <span class='line-break'> </span> with Edna's help.  I got <span class='line-break'> </span> supper.  Mabel is sick to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Hope she will be well by morning.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2144">
<h3><a name="page-2144">Wednesday, September  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> some apples to John Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> and ground them for cider. <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim made a hog trough this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Corn is out at our <span class='line-break'> </span> house.  Nellie worked on some<span class='line-break'> </span> waists for Franklin today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny made Edna some <span class='line-break'> </span> bloomers yesterday.  A col[oured] <span class='line-break'> </span> girl and I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie made the bread for <span class='line-break'> </span> supper and milked with <span class='line-break'> </span> Edna's help.  Daisy the col[oured]<span class='line-break'> </span> girl and I picked a few<span class='line-break'> </span> peas this evening.  Mabel has bin as well as <span class='line-break'> </span> usual to day.  I got <span class='line-break'> </span> some nice sweet potatoes <span class='line-break'> </span> today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2145">
<h3><a name="page-2145">Thursday, September  7, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Ben moved <span class='line-break'> </span> some tobacco this morning.  This <span class='line-break'> </span> evening Ben carried three<span class='line-break'> </span> of the children and I to <span class='line-break'> </span> White Falls.  I caught 28<span class='line-break'> </span> fish.  Henry drove the team<span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill except the hill <span class='line-break'> </span> leading to the mill at the cork <span class='line-break'> </span> mill.  We had a good time.  <span class='line-break'> </span> The children done fine for <span class='line-break'> </span> them. Grace &amp; May Brumfield <span class='line-break'> </span> and two children come while <span class='line-break'> </span> I was gone.  I would of bin  <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to see them.  I am glad that <span class='line-break'> </span> they come to see Josie anyway.<span class='line-break'> </span> Daisy the col[oured] girl and I went <span class='line-break'> </span> to washing this morning.  Queen <span class='line-break'> </span> Callans come to wash.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I let her &amp; Daisy wash a [beg?].<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2146">
<h3><a name="page-2146">Friday, September  8, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Well another day has gone. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry went to Gretna <span class='line-break'> </span> to carrie Marvin Smiths rake <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; mower.  They have just got <span class='line-break'> </span> home nine at night.  Jim worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on a hog lot most of the day. <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie helped him move a <span class='line-break'> </span> little tobacco this morning. Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Edna milked last night &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning &amp; tonight.  I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Daisy ironed some. <span class='line-break'> </span> She washed for her self <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Mollie Reynols <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Johnson come after <span class='line-break'> </span> her.  Josie has suffered <span class='line-break'> </span> a lot today.  Nellie got a <span class='line-break'> </span> letter from Eylin tonight. <span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad that she got [it]. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2147">
<h3><a name="page-2147">Saturday, September  9, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very hot day.  Daisy <span class='line-break'> </span> and I ironed most of the <span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Daisy washed the <span class='line-break'> </span> cook room this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I mended some over alls <span class='line-break'> </span> and sewed on a few <span class='line-break'> </span> buttons.  Nellie sewed on <span class='line-break'> </span> buttons and made two under <span class='line-break'> </span> waists.  The men folks cut <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; set up corn this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> The little (col)[sic] children <span class='line-break'> </span> picked some peas.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Ben &amp; Henry went to <span class='line-break'> </span> the barn tonight to make <span class='line-break'> </span> fines.  Mabel slept this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening and now she<span class='line-break'> </span> is wide awake and I <span class='line-break'> </span> wish she would not make <span class='line-break'> </span> so much fuss.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2148">
<h3><a name="page-2148">Sunday, September 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Very warm.  We <span class='line-break'> </span> all staid about home but  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Cedar Forest <span class='line-break'> </span> for Mrs Car.  They went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Rob Hubbards and spent <span class='line-break'> </span> the day. They got home a <span class='line-break'> </span> bout night.  Lizzie &amp; Alma<span class='line-break'> </span> and Gordon &amp; family all <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has felt some better <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I and a col[oured] girl <span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner today.  I churned.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Power went joy <span class='line-break'> </span> rideing this morning with <span class='line-break'> </span> [Orvel?]&amp; Jamie Gravely.  This <span class='line-break'> </span> evening they went to Gretna.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie is a fine girl I think. <span class='line-break'> </span> She has waited on Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> faithful all this week.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2149">
<h3><a name="page-2149">Monday, September 11, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning rain this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  We were going to <span class='line-break'> </span> the Store &amp; mill so as to <span class='line-break'> </span> fish and it rained.  Then it <span class='line-break'> </span> cleared up and we went.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> fished a little while and then <span class='line-break'> </span> I decided it was going to <span class='line-break'> </span> rain a gain so we started for <span class='line-break'> </span> home.  We stopped at Thomsons <span class='line-break'> </span> Store a while and when we <span class='line-break'> </span> started a gain the rain met<span class='line-break'> </span> us.  We all got wet eneough<span class='line-break'> </span> to have to change clothes.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> hope it wont hurt none of <span class='line-break'> </span> us.  All of the children was <span class='line-break'> </span> with us.  All of them at <span class='line-break'> </span> home staid dry but Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Nel.  She was milking and got <span class='line-break'> </span> wet.  She was not well.  I hope it wont hurt her.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2150">
<h3><a name="page-2150">Tuesday, September 12, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim and Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> cut &amp; shocked corn today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie has bin complaining<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  Daisy and I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Denia Blair <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie today. <span class='line-break'> </span> I went with her as far <span class='line-break'> </span> as the pea patch.  Could not <span class='line-break'> </span> get green peas eneough<span class='line-break'> </span> to make a [meer?].  I come <span class='line-break'> </span> by Mrs Booker.  I got <span class='line-break'> </span> peas eneough to cook.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim drove up <span class='line-break'> </span> my cow this morning.  I milked <span class='line-break'> </span> her tonight.  I got some <span class='line-break'> </span> potatoe vines for the cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Edmons &amp; Mrs Edmons <span class='line-break'> </span> was passing.  They brought the <span class='line-break'> </span> vines for me. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2151">
<h3><a name="page-2151">Wednesday, September 13, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  The <span class='line-break'> </span> men cut corn.  The <span class='line-break'> </span> children went to school. <span class='line-break'> </span> School commened at Renan <span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  Nellie &amp; Edna done<span class='line-break'> </span> the milking.  Daisy and I <span class='line-break'> </span> done the cooking.  Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> staid with Mrs Car <span class='line-break'> </span> most of the morning. <span class='line-break'> </span> John Hutchersons children <span class='line-break'> </span> come this evening and got <span class='line-break'> </span> twe kittens.  I hope they can <span class='line-break'> </span> rais them.  [Ella?] Mayhew <span class='line-break'> </span> come a little while and <span class='line-break'> </span> played with the children. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie was very sick today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Mrs Hendricks<span class='line-break'> </span> and got her some ice. <span class='line-break'> </span> He went quick.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2152">
<h3><a name="page-2152">Thursday, September 14, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The men cut corn. <span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school. <span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner &amp; churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie milked and caned <span class='line-break'> </span> some apples &amp; made jellie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Daisy &amp; Queen both (col[oured)]<span class='line-break'> </span> washed.  Mrs Dr Owen <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie a<span class='line-break'> </span> while this evening.  Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> has bin lead off all day.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Power come <span class='line-break'> </span> back tonight.  Miss Janie <span class='line-break'> </span> Gravely come with <span class='line-break'> </span> her.  She did not stay <span class='line-break'> </span> but a few minutes.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel has bin good<span class='line-break'> </span> all day today.  I broke <span class='line-break'> </span> my glasses to day.  A Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Layne come here begging today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p>   </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2153">
<h3><a name="page-2153">Friday, September 15, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  I was at home this morning and got <span class='line-break'> </span> most of the breakfast.  <span class='line-break'> </span> After breakfast Ben said <span class='line-break'> </span> he would carrie me to Gretna <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; to Carries and I could <span class='line-break'> </span> stay until Sunday.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> ready as fast as I could <span class='line-break'> </span> and we went.  He carried <span class='line-break'> </span> the children as far as the <span class='line-break'> </span> school house.  I went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Carries at ten oclock.  Fond <span class='line-break'> </span> them weel.  I eat dinner <span class='line-break'> </span> and worked some button <span class='line-break'> </span> holes in Carries baby's aprons.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Had a good evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Thought a bout them <span class='line-break'> </span> at home a lot while I <span class='line-break'> </span> was a way.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2154">
<h3><a name="page-2154">Saturday, September 16, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  I am at [marv..].<span class='line-break'> </span> We eat breakfast and <span class='line-break'> </span> Corrie got dinner.  Reese<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at Altavista all night<span class='line-break'> </span> at Dr Smiths.  He had bin <span class='line-break'> </span> to Lynchburg and had <span class='line-break'> </span> his eyes <span class='line-break'> </span> examined.  He come a bout <span class='line-break'> </span> 9 oclock.  We got bait <span class='line-break'> </span> and went to Owens <span class='line-break'> </span> pond. We caught some <span class='line-break'> </span> fish.  We come home and <span class='line-break'> </span> eat dinner then went <span class='line-break'> </span> Galveston and fished a <span class='line-break'> </span> while.  Come to Gretna <span class='line-break'> </span> and stoped.  Bought<span class='line-break'> </span> several things and <span class='line-break'> </span> went home.  There was <span class='line-break'> </span> a cloud in the night thundered and rained a little.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2155">
<h3><a name="page-2155">Sunday, September 17, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day I am at Carries <span class='line-break'> </span> but must go home today. <span class='line-break'> </span> John &amp; Christenia Brumfield <span class='line-break'> </span> come to Marvins to see me. <span class='line-break'> </span> They did stay long.  I was glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that they come.  After they <span class='line-break'> </span> went Carrie &amp; I walked <span class='line-break'> </span> a round some.  Went to see <span class='line-break'> </span> the ice pond and the nice <span class='line-break'> </span> apples in the young orchard<span class='line-break'> </span> then went home and eat <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Then come home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie and all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> come home with me.  Fond <span class='line-break'> </span> all well and doing well<span class='line-break'> </span> but Josie.  She is very bad <span class='line-break'> </span> off.  Evry thing looks like <span class='line-break'> </span> they did not miss me.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> milked to night.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2156">
<h3><a name="page-2156">Monday, September 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben disked<span class='line-break'> </span> land for oats.  Jim fixed up <span class='line-break'> </span> the shed ready for stripping <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Max Car went from <span class='line-break'> </span> here today.  Kate Harvey <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I went to George Blairs. <span class='line-break'> </span> The girls was at home. <span class='line-break'> </span> Their mother was gone to <span class='line-break'> </span> Altavista to hear Billie <span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday preach.  Otho &amp; Sallie <span class='line-break'> </span> went.  Otho drove the car. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ann Coles &amp; Ellen Lewis<span class='line-break'> </span> washed for the Blairs. <span class='line-break'> </span> I was so glad to see <span class='line-break'> </span> them all again.  Ben has <span class='line-break'> </span> gone hunting to night. <span class='line-break'> </span> The weather is cool to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.   <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2157">
<h3><a name="page-2157">Tuesday, September 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> a little tobacco.  Ben disked <span class='line-break'> </span> his land for oats.  Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> made some pickle and <span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner with Daisys<span class='line-break'> </span> help.  Queen washed to <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  I went to Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> and spent most of the <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Jim Thomson &amp; family <span class='line-break'> </span> come down there.  Jim helped <span class='line-break'> </span> set up corn.  Alice and <span class='line-break'> </span> the children &amp; Mildred <span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson come here to see <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie.  [Ila?] &amp; Cordie come <span class='line-break'> </span> to see Mrs Booker.  She was <span class='line-break'> </span> not at the house and they <span class='line-break'> </span> come down here.  Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson come to her <span class='line-break'> </span> fathers today.  Effie B come to spend the night. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2158">
<h3><a name="page-2158">Wednesday, September 20, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Long Island for guano.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim stripped tobacco <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie got dinner.  Daisy <span class='line-break'> </span> ironed.  I went with Johnson <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Mollie to the island.  I fished. <span class='line-break'> </span> Did not catch any thing<span class='line-break'> </span> worth keeping.  We eat <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner at Cedar Forest. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie had a good lunch.<span class='line-break'> </span> John &amp; Edwin come to see <span class='line-break'> </span> us a little while. Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie went with them<span class='line-break'> </span> back to Gretna on their way<span class='line-break'> </span> to Chatham.  [Evrylin?] is at <span class='line-break'> </span> home. Mrs Mayhew &amp; Rena <span class='line-break'> </span> come a little while this eve.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie has gone to Kate <span class='line-break'> </span> Harveys to night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2159">
<h3><a name="page-2159">Thursday, September 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> tried to start the [lig..?] <span class='line-break'> </span> engine and could not <span class='line-break'> </span> get it to work.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> carried Mabel and I <span class='line-break'> </span> to White Falls. I<span class='line-break'> </span> caught 18 fish.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> know that Ben is <span class='line-break'> </span> tired of me bothering <span class='line-break'> </span> him about going.<span class='line-break'> </span> I work for him and <span class='line-break'> </span> his family and dont <span class='line-break'> </span> get thanked for it. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie is feeling very <span class='line-break'> </span> bad.  Fanny got supper <span class='line-break'> </span> and all of them eat<span class='line-break'> </span> while I was milking.  <span class='line-break'> </span> This is guess work writing.<span class='line-break'> </span>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2160">
<h3><a name="page-2160">Friday, September 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben disked.  He had <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Edmons disk.  Jim come home <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  I got dinner. Daisy<span class='line-break'> </span> col girl washed some this <span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Mr Rufus Car &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> family come to see Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Kate Harvey &amp; Julia <span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson come this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Heard to day that John &amp; Edwin <span class='line-break'> </span> started to Washington today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Miss Janie Gravely &amp; her <span class='line-break'> </span> friend come in a few <span class='line-break'> </span> minutes this evening.  Fanny <span class='line-break'> </span> Power went with them <span class='line-break'> </span> home. They expect company <span class='line-break'> </span> there tonight.  Heard tonight <span class='line-break'> </span> that Ray Booker is sick. <span class='line-break'> </span> He has diphtheria.  I hope he <span class='line-break'> </span> may soon be well. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2161">
<h3><a name="page-2161">Saturday, September 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben worked <span class='line-break'> </span> on his wheat land.  Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  Fanny <span class='line-break'> </span> went home. I am sorry for  <span class='line-break'> </span> we will miss her so much. <span class='line-break'> </span> She was so good to wait <span class='line-break'> </span> on Josie.  Ray Booker <span class='line-break'> </span> is very sick.  I went up <span class='line-break'> </span> there this evening to see <span class='line-break'> </span> him.  Dr Owen &amp; Dr Shelton <span class='line-break'> </span> are there tonight.  I do hope <span class='line-break'> </span> that he may get well. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry went <span class='line-break'> </span> hunting to night. Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr Bookers. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie went in the <span class='line-break'> </span> Parlor this evening. Fanny <span class='line-break'> </span> helped her to go in and <span class='line-break'> </span> come out.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2162">
<h3><a name="page-2162">Sunday, September 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at home until <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Then they went <span class='line-break'> </span> to look for fallen <span class='line-break'> </span> apples.  They found <span class='line-break'> </span> some.  Daisy and I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. I bathed the <span class='line-break'> </span> children Mabel &amp; [F....?] <span class='line-break'> </span> Late this evening Tim <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Lizzie and Henry Blair <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; his wife &amp; Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hendrix come.  Lizzie <span class='line-break'> </span> stayed all night and <span class='line-break'> </span> will stay this week.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad Ray <span class='line-break'> </span> Booker is some better. <span class='line-break'> </span> I hope he will get well<span class='line-break'> </span> soon.  Henry went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Renan this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2163">
<h3><a name="page-2163">Monday, September 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A fine day.  Cool tonight.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben worked on the <span class='line-break'> </span> oat land.  [I?] Some chaps <span class='line-break'> </span> shucked a shock of corn <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and put it  <span class='line-break'> </span> in the corn house.  I and <span class='line-break'> </span> the col girl  got dinner.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I churned this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to the island<span class='line-break'> </span> for grass seed. Mabel <span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with him. <span class='line-break'> </span> I fished a little while. <span class='line-break'> </span> Caught two little fish.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie helped get supper <span class='line-break'> </span> while I milked the cows. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim &amp; Rob<span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard has gone <span class='line-break'> </span> hunting tonight.  Dont know <span class='line-break'> </span> when they will get home.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2164">
<h3><a name="page-2164">Tuesday, September 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> worked on their grain land <span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  Robbert Hubbard <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; wife went from here <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Carrie &amp; the <span class='line-break'> </span> children come this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad to see them. <span class='line-break'> </span> I hope they got home <span class='line-break'> </span> safe.  Lizzie and I and the  <span class='line-break'> </span> col girl shelled some <span class='line-break'> </span> corn to dry out to send <span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill.  We want <span class='line-break'> </span> corn bread.  Lizzie and I <span class='line-break'> </span> went to the [?] house<span class='line-break'> </span> to get potatoes and peas <span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner.  I went to <span class='line-break'> </span> the barn to get sweet <span class='line-break'> </span> potatoes.  Mr Kent carried <span class='line-break'> </span> the children part way to school.<span class='line-break'> </span>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2165">
<h3><a name="page-2165">Wednesday, September 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys sowed <span class='line-break'> </span> oats today.  Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna.  Mabel and I went <span class='line-break'> </span> with him.  Mabel was very <span class='line-break'> </span> good for her.  We staid <span class='line-break'> </span> nearly all the evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben had some work <span class='line-break'> </span> done on his batteries. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie was here this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried her home &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie went with her. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has felt very bad<span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  I have had <span class='line-break'> </span> corn out drying today. <span class='line-break'> </span> I done nearly all about <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Lizzie churned <span class='line-break'> </span> for me and helped<span class='line-break'> </span> me do what I was doing. <span class='line-break'> </span> Daisy is very good help.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2166">
<h3><a name="page-2166">Thursday, September 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben cut peas <span class='line-break'> </span> for Kate today.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Jim &amp; Ben both <span class='line-break'> </span> tied some tonight.  Lizzie <span class='line-break'> </span> is here again tonight.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> am glad for her to be <span class='line-break'> </span> here.  Daisy ironed some <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  I got most <span class='line-break'> </span> of dinner &amp; churned.  <span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school. I went this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening and gathered <span class='line-break'> </span> some peas &amp; got some <span class='line-break'> </span> potatoes for tomorrows <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I got a letter<span class='line-break'> </span> from Carrie.  Was glad <span class='line-break'> </span> to hear from them.  Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> had to write a letter <span class='line-break'> </span> tonight. Henry has gone hunting.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2167">
<h3><a name="page-2167">Friday, September 29, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> some tobacco.  Ben went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna with Mr Mayhew.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Come home before twelve. <span class='line-break'> </span> Commenced to make a tongue <span class='line-break'> </span> for the roller.  Went <span class='line-break'> </span> to the mill with a little <span class='line-break'> </span> corn.  He carried all of <span class='line-break'> </span> the children and I went two.<span class='line-break'> </span> I fished some. Caught <span class='line-break'> </span> 13 fish.  Denia &amp; Kate<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie. Irvin  <span class='line-break'> </span> Harvey come to see her two.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie Bennett got supper<span class='line-break'> </span> for me tonight.  We had <span class='line-break'> </span> beef steak.  Frank Blair <span class='line-break'> </span> and his mother come tonight<span class='line-break'> </span> in the car for Lizzie.  Jim &amp; Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Henry went to the school house. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2168">
<h3><a name="page-2168">Saturday, September 30, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Ben worked on a roller <span class='line-break'> </span> all the morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> he carried Daisy the col <span class='line-break'> </span> girl home.  All the children <span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with him.<span class='line-break'> </span> He was in a fret all the <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  I think now that I <span class='line-break'> </span> never will ask him to take<span class='line-break'> </span> me any where a gain.<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie come here this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Denia come with her but <span class='line-break'> </span> would not come in the house.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Staid and talked until a <span class='line-break'> </span> bout dinner time.  Lizzie <span class='line-break'> </span> baked a cake to day. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie had a flighty spell<span class='line-break'> </span> a gain this evening.  Mollie <span class='line-break'> </span> was to see her this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2169">
<h3><a name="page-2169">Sunday, October  1, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> and Ben staid at home <span class='line-break'> </span> all day.  Lizzie was here.  <span class='line-break'> </span> she helped me get dinner. <span class='line-break'> </span> We cooked Turnip salit<span class='line-break'> </span> and a chicken.  We had a <span class='line-break'> </span> nice cake.  Today was Mabel's <span class='line-break'> </span> Birth day.  She is three years<span class='line-break'> </span> olde.  This evening Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Elsie East &amp; Gladis <span class='line-break'> </span> Brumfield come a few <span class='line-break'> </span> minutes.  Tim Bennett &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Gordon &amp; [Chesley?] Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; a Mr Hedrick come <span class='line-break'> </span> by for Lizzie. I did <span class='line-break'> </span> hate for her to go home <span class='line-break'> </span> as we have not got any <span class='line-break'> </span> body to help to do the <span class='line-break'> </span> work here now.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2170">
<h3><a name="page-2170">Monday, October  2, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben run the light <span class='line-break'> </span> engine a while today.  Rolled the <span class='line-break'> </span> oat land some.  This evening <span class='line-break'> </span> he went for a coloured girl.<span class='line-break'> </span> She come.  I hope I will like <span class='line-break'> </span> her.  Mrs Doss come to see Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Ella come tonight. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ray Hubbard brought her.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim has stripped tobacco <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Mabel and I went<span class='line-break'> </span> with Ben as far as the Bridge <span class='line-break'> </span> at Stankeys.  I got very <span class='line-break'> </span> impatient waiting for Ben.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel was good all the evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ray Hubbard brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie some nice tomatoes. <span class='line-break'> </span> Jessie sent her a Jar <span class='line-break'> </span> of pickle.  Evry one is <span class='line-break'> </span> so good to her.  She is thankful.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2171">
<h3><a name="page-2171">Tuesday, October  3, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben raked up <span class='line-break'> </span> Kates pea hay today.  Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped some tobacco. <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie Brumfield and Evylin<span class='line-break'> </span> and her husband and Mr <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Mrs Gyer &amp; baby come. <span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad that they did. <span class='line-break'> </span> They had dinner with <span class='line-break'> </span> them &amp; eat before they come. <span class='line-break'> </span> I could of gave them dinner <span class='line-break'> </span> ok as I have help.  Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> has bin a bout as usual<span class='line-break'> </span> today and that is bad. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Edmons come in a <span class='line-break'> </span> few minutes this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> They are carrying on <span class='line-break'> </span> a meeting at Strait Stone.<span class='line-break'> </span> Queen Callans washed <span class='line-break'> </span> here today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2172">
<h3><a name="page-2172">Wednesday, October  4, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  We need rain very <span class='line-break'> </span> bad.  Jim &amp; Ben got up Kates <span class='line-break'> </span> pea hay this evening.  I am so <span class='line-break'> </span> glad that it is up.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Bettie a col girl<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed.  Ben carried Ella <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard to Mr Towers <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Mollie Rey[nolds?] <span class='line-break'> </span> was here this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has suffered most <span class='line-break'> </span> of the day.  Jim plowed <span class='line-break'> </span> up the potatoes this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  They are to pick<span class='line-break'> </span> up now.  William sent <span class='line-break'> </span> the buggy home this evening <span class='line-break'> </span> by his children.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel has a colde. Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> is getting her lesson 8 oclock.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Heard today that Effie has a little girl<span class='line-break'> </span> Born Sep the 30th Josie Gunn.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2173">
<h3><a name="page-2173">Thursday, October  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben made a box <span class='line-break'> </span> for William Gilbert to bury <span class='line-break'> </span> his baby in.  Jim got up <span class='line-break'> </span> the sweet potatoes and pop <span class='line-break'> </span> corn.  I got dinner.  Betty <span class='line-break'> </span> ironed some &amp; washed some.  <span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I went with <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr &amp; Mrs Edmons to church. <span class='line-break'> </span> I am very glad for any <span class='line-break'> </span> one to take me with them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Archer Thornton &amp; Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Rufus Car &amp; children come <span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie &amp; the children &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate come a few minutes. <span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad to see them.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went with Mr <span class='line-break'> </span> Edmons folk to Strait Stone <span class='line-break'> </span> to night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2174">
<h3><a name="page-2174">Friday, October  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> finish cutting corn. Betty<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed all the morning.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Mrs Edmons <span class='line-break'> </span> carried me with them to <span class='line-break'> </span> meeting.  Henry has gone <span class='line-break'> </span> to meeting tonight.  I like to <span class='line-break'> </span> go and meet the old &amp; young <span class='line-break'> </span> that I know.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin [pent?] all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie come to see Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Jim has shucked <span class='line-break'> </span> some popcorn.  He shucked <span class='line-break'> </span> it at night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2175">
<h3><a name="page-2175">Saturday, October  7, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning.  The rain <span class='line-break'> </span> was badly needed.  Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry stripped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day finished Jim's<span class='line-break'> </span> cureing and loaded it on the <span class='line-break'> </span> waggon. Mr Booker &amp; Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> put their tobacco on Mr Bookers <span class='line-break'> </span> waggon.  Ben &amp; Jim has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to Renan &amp; Dr Owens <span class='line-break'> </span> for medicine.  I went to <span class='line-break'> </span> see Mrs Hutcherson this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  She is very sick <span class='line-break'> </span> but feeling some better. <span class='line-break'> </span> Denia was there.  Ada &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Denia was sheling peas. <span class='line-break'> </span> Miss Ada brought me <span class='line-break'> </span> home on Mrs Hutcherson's car.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad to get home so <span class='line-break'> </span> easy.  Mabel has had a good time today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2176">
<h3><a name="page-2176">Sunday, October  8, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day most of the day. <span class='line-break'> </span> Rained last night.  Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Ben staid at home all <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  I got the most of <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Betty helped me <span class='line-break'> </span> some.  I churned.  Mr Booker <span class='line-break'> </span> carried me to Strait <span class='line-break'> </span> Stone to the Baptizeing. <span class='line-break'> </span> There was a lot of <span class='line-break'> </span> little girls and some <span class='line-break'> </span> boys and two men baptized. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ther was a big crowd <span class='line-break'> </span> there.  Mrs Edmons <span class='line-break'> </span> brought me home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went down <span class='line-break'> </span> there tonight.  Josie is <span class='line-break'> </span> suffering awful tonight. <span class='line-break'> </span> Oh that we could help <span class='line-break'> </span> her. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2177">
<h3><a name="page-2177">Monday, October  9, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A bad day.  Jim &amp; Mr Booker <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna. They have <span class='line-break'> </span> got back as far as Mr Bookers.<span class='line-break'> </span> It is raining so hard that <span class='line-break'> </span> any one would get wet <span class='line-break'> </span> in a few minutes.  I did <span class='line-break'> </span> not milk but one cow <span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  The children <span class='line-break'> </span> are at the dineing room <span class='line-break'> </span> getting their lessons.  Fanny <span class='line-break'> </span> Power is with them.  She <span class='line-break'> </span> come up here last night <span class='line-break'> </span> from church.  Henry made <span class='line-break'> </span> a proffession last night and <span class='line-break'> </span> joined the church.  Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> has not suffered so much<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Ben commenced to <span class='line-break'> </span> strip tobacco today. <span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2178">
<h3><a name="page-2178">Tuesday, October 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy morning clear to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Jim &amp; Ben stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco today.  Rob Hubbard <span class='line-break'> </span> is here tonight.  He has come <span class='line-break'> </span> for a cow.  Bettie the col<span class='line-break'> </span> girl is sick tonight.  Josie has <span class='line-break'> </span> bin feeling some better <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Rufus &amp; Mamie <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Kent come a few <span class='line-break'> </span> minutes this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Rob brought tomatoes &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Rufus brought <span class='line-break'> </span> celery.  Mamie brought <span class='line-break'> </span> potatoe salid.  I had a <span class='line-break'> </span> letter from Carrie today. <span class='line-break'> </span> I am always glad to <span class='line-break'> </span> hear from them.  Bruce [Rey]<span class='line-break'> </span> was married Oct 7th 1922.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2179">
<h3><a name="page-2179">Wednesday, October 11, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear day.  Ben &amp; Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco today. <span class='line-break'> </span> I gathered some peas for <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  No one come <span class='line-break'> </span> until late this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Then Carrie &amp; the children <span class='line-break'> </span> and Nellie come.  Carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> did not stay but a <span class='line-break'> </span> little while.  Nellie will <span class='line-break'> </span> stay a while.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Josie has suffered very <span class='line-break'> </span> much today.  Today is <span class='line-break'> </span> Henry's birth day.  He is <span class='line-break'> </span> 13 years old.  I went <span class='line-break'> </span> to the orchard and got <span class='line-break'> </span> some apples.  I guess a <span class='line-break'> </span> hawk got one of my <span class='line-break'> </span> chickens today.  It is <span class='line-break'> </span> missing any way.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2180">
<h3><a name="page-2180">Thursday, October 12, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> on Henry's tobacco &amp; finished<span class='line-break'> </span> it and loaded it on the car.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Then heard that there was so <span class='line-break'> </span> much tobacco on the market<span class='line-break'> </span> that they could not hendle <span class='line-break'> </span> it.  They unloaded it and <span class='line-break'> </span> packed down in the barn.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben carried Mrs Car to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna this evening on her <span class='line-break'> </span> way to Lynchburg.  I hope <span class='line-break'> </span> she may get there ok.<span class='line-break'> </span> Queen Callans washed <span class='line-break'> </span> here today.  Heard today <span class='line-break'> </span> that a collored woman<span class='line-break'> </span> died at Mr Hutcherson's.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Renols come <span class='line-break'> </span> a little while this evening. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben's dog come home.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2181">
<h3><a name="page-2181">Friday, October 13, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco at the <span class='line-break'> </span> barn in the woods until <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Then Ben carried <span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel and I to White <span class='line-break'> </span> Falls.  I caught 8 fish.  <span class='line-break'> </span> When we got home the <span class='line-break'> </span> col girl wanted to go home.  <span class='line-break'> </span> He carried her home.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie preserved &amp; caned <span class='line-break'> </span> some pears today and <span class='line-break'> </span> gathered green tomatoes <span class='line-break'> </span> to make pickle.  Bettie <span class='line-break'> </span> ironed most of the day.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie had bin [pent?] of day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jo Edmons &amp; Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> has gone hunting to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Jim &amp; Ben has gone <span class='line-break'> </span> to the barn to strip tobacco.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2182">
<h3><a name="page-2182">Saturday, October 14, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Cloudy all the <span class='line-break'> </span> evening &amp; rain tonight.  Jim &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben stripped tobacco until <span class='line-break'> </span> twelve then Jim carried <span class='line-break'> </span> a few apples to Hutchersons <span class='line-break'> </span> and ground them.  Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Gretna <span class='line-break'> </span> to meet Mrs Car.  She did <span class='line-break'> </span> not come.  WE are all sorry.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny bathed Franklin &amp; Mabel.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Kate Harvey &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Grace Brumfield Lottie Kelly <span class='line-break'> </span> and Sally Blair come to <span class='line-break'> </span> see Josie.  I am glad that <span class='line-break'> </span> they come.  I would of bin <span class='line-break'> </span> glad to seen them all<span class='line-break'> </span> but there was some thing <span class='line-break'> </span> that I wanted.  Nellie put <span class='line-break'> </span> up some pickle this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2183">
<h3><a name="page-2183">Sunday, October 15, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day &amp; some rain. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry went to Strait <span class='line-break'> </span> Stone to meeting &amp; Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> was baptized.  Nellie and <span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  We had beef <span class='line-break'> </span> steak with onions in it.  <span class='line-break'> </span> I went to Mollie Reynols.  <span class='line-break'> </span> There was no one at home.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Then I went to Renan.  All<span class='line-break'> </span> the Reynols was at Clack <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbards. While I was <span class='line-break'> </span> there Paul Bennett &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Faber Jefferson &amp; wife <span class='line-break'> </span> and children &amp; Alma Bennet<span class='line-break'> </span> come by and stopped <span class='line-break'> </span> to patch a time and we <span class='line-break'> </span> all talked a while.  I went <span class='line-break'> </span> over to see Kate Harvey a <span class='line-break'> </span> few minutes. Julia Fergerson come a few minutes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2184">
<h3><a name="page-2184">Monday, October 16, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy and some rain.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim stripped tobacco. <span class='line-break'> </span> Tobacco is very high in order.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin suffering all day to <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Ben went to Hutchersons <span class='line-break'> </span> for tablets that they got at <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna.  The children went <span class='line-break'> </span> to school.  Nellie and <span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  We cooked <span class='line-break'> </span> peas and turnip salit &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> baked potatoes.  I went <span class='line-break'> </span> to the barn for the first <span class='line-break'> </span> time since the tobacco was<span class='line-break'> </span> cured.  Fanny Power went <span class='line-break'> </span> home.  We miss her so <span class='line-break'> </span> much. Mabel had a <span class='line-break'> </span> nap of sleep today and <span class='line-break'> </span> she cant go to sleep <span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2185">
<h3><a name="page-2185">Tuesday, October 17, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day but no <span class='line-break'> </span> rain.  Ben &amp; Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day &amp; tonight <span class='line-break'> </span> they tieing.  I and Mabel went <span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr Booker.  They were <span class='line-break'> </span> at the Barn at work on <span class='line-break'> </span> their tobacco.  Josie has bin <span class='line-break'> </span> feeling some better today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie &amp; I got dinner. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Lipscome &amp; Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Lipscome come to see <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> We finished putting <span class='line-break'> </span> up the sweet potatoes<span class='line-break'> </span> today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Queen washed here<span class='line-break'> </span> today.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2186">
<h3><a name="page-2186">Wednesday, October 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped some tobacco.  Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> shod the horses this morning.  <span class='line-break'> </span> This evening late he went <span class='line-break'> </span> for a col girl.  She come. <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin very bad off <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  No one come to see her <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  She got a box of flower[?] <span class='line-break'> </span> through the mail. Got a <span class='line-break'> </span> letter from Carrie this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Was so glad to <span class='line-break'> </span> hear from them. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben intended loadeing<span class='line-break'> </span> his tobacco and going <span class='line-break'> </span> to Gretna tomorrow <span class='line-break'> </span> but he heard that <span class='line-break'> </span> they had more there than<span class='line-break'> </span> they could handle so he <span class='line-break'> </span> did not try to go. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2187">
<h3><a name="page-2187">Thursday, October 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear cool day some frost <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> loaded the waggon with Bens <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Henrys tobacco and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin bad off all<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Mr Power phoned that<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie would come here if Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> would come after her.  Ben was gone <span class='line-break'> </span> so we though we would get <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Booker to go for her. Mr Kellie <span class='line-break'> </span> was at Mr Booker and said he <span class='line-break'> </span> would go and he went made a <span class='line-break'> </span> quick trip.  I am so glad she is <span class='line-break'> </span> here.  Late this evening Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson &amp; Lottie Kellie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Ehel Worsham &amp; Denia<span class='line-break'> </span> Blair come and staid a<span class='line-break'> </span> little while.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2188">
<h3><a name="page-2188">Friday, October 20, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna.  Ben solde <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Was very well pleased.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben got Marvins auto and <span class='line-break'> </span> come home last night.  Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> has not suffered as much <span class='line-break'> </span> today as she does some day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Booker come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie this evening.  Mr Kellie<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Josie a nice box<span class='line-break'> </span> of good things to eat today.<span class='line-break'> </span> They have bin good to Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; so have all the people<span class='line-break'> </span> a round.  Kate was here <span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> She wanted a few chickens.<span class='line-break'> </span> I have caught 4 tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben wants to commence<span class='line-break'> </span> getting land ready to sow wheat.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2189">
<h3><a name="page-2189">Saturday, October 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Henry disked land<span class='line-break'> </span> for wheat.  Ben put shoes <span class='line-break'> </span> on his horse then he carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna &amp; I to the river.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> fished.  Edna caught three<span class='line-break'> </span> fish.  Ben carried us and he<span class='line-break'> </span> come home &amp; then come after<span class='line-break'> </span> us brought us home and <span class='line-break'> </span> then went to Gretna and<span class='line-break'> </span> back by late supper and<span class='line-break'> </span> now he is at the barn tieing<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Jim &amp; Nellie are tieing<span class='line-break'> </span> two [sic].  Nellie &amp; Bettie got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner &amp; supper.  I milked<span class='line-break'> </span> the cows.  Josie is very bad<span class='line-break'> </span> off.  They carried me fishing <span class='line-break'> </span> because they know I am olde<span class='line-break'> </span> that I never will go many more times.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2190">
<h3><a name="page-2190">Sunday, October 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben staid <span class='line-break'> </span> at home all day.  Mr Sam <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard &amp; Mrs Mrs Rob &amp; Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Carington &amp; Miss Anna all <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbards come to see Josie <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Carrie Smith <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Marvin and all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> come a little while. <span class='line-break'> </span> I went to George Blairs<span class='line-break'> </span> and eat dinner.  They had a <span class='line-break'> </span> lot of company all kinds<span class='line-break'> </span> folks except Mrs Hutcherson<span class='line-break'> </span> And Miss T....?Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Sunday School and then<span class='line-break'> </span> to George Blairs. Lottie <span class='line-break'> </span> Craddock combed my hair<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I am glad to be remembered that much.<span class='line-break'> </span> Today is my birth day.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> 76 years olde.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2191">
<h3><a name="page-2191">Monday, October 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning.  Rain this <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Ben worked on <span class='line-break'> </span> his wheat land until it<span class='line-break'> </span> rained.  He fixed to plant <span class='line-break'> </span> some bulbs.  I planted <span class='line-break'> </span> a few hyacinths.  I sent <span class='line-break'> </span> for the News today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Nellie tied some <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Nellie washed some this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Josie has not<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered quite as much<span class='line-break'> </span> today as she does some days.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry carried 4 chickens <span class='line-break'> </span> to Kate Harveys this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> He bought 4 steel traps.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2192">
<h3><a name="page-2192">Tuesday, October 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim and Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school. Nellie sewed <span class='line-break'> </span> some.  Queen washed here<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Carrie Smith come <span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes.  I am <span class='line-break'> </span> always so glad to see <span class='line-break'> </span> her.  She had a part of <span class='line-break'> </span> the children with <span class='line-break'> </span> her.  Mollie Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> come a little while this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  I planted <span class='line-break'> </span> some bulbs this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben has had the prettys<span class='line-break'> </span> flower garden this year<span class='line-break'> </span> that I ever saw.  Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> has bin with me most of <span class='line-break'> </span> the evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2193">
<h3><a name="page-2193">Wednesday, October 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben hauled<span class='line-break'> </span> some wood this morning &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> worked on his wheat land <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Jim &amp; Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Bettie and I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> We cooked turnip <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; peas and potatoes. This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> I cut the Morning Glorie<span class='line-break'> </span> vine off of the garden fence <span class='line-break'> </span> and then went to Renan<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; to see Kate Harvey carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> the money to pay my taxes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Mayhew was at the <span class='line-break'> </span> store on his machine and <span class='line-break'> </span> brough me home.  I was <span class='line-break'> </span> glad that I did not have <span class='line-break'> </span> to walk. Ben &amp; Jim is at<span class='line-break'> </span> the barn putting tobacco in the pit. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2194">
<h3><a name="page-2194">Thursday, October 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear cool day.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Nellie stripped tobacco.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben sowed wheat finished <span class='line-break'> </span> what he expected to sow.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Bettie ironed.  I got the <span class='line-break'> </span> most of the dinner.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Mayhew sent Josie some<span class='line-break'> </span> flowers by the school<span class='line-break'> </span> children.  I gathered a <span class='line-break'> </span> few violets this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> MRs Edmons come to see <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie this evening.  I cut the <span class='line-break'> </span> Morning Glorie vine from <span class='line-break'> </span> garden fence yesterday and<span class='line-break'> </span> fed it to the cows today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> barn tonight to hang tobacco.  Henry <span class='line-break'> </span> has gone hunting.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2195">
<h3><a name="page-2195">Friday, October 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  Jim &amp; Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco all day Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> a part of the day.  Willie <span class='line-break'> </span> Bobbett come this morning <span class='line-break'> </span> and bought a calf.  He paid <span class='line-break'> </span> five dollars for it. That <span class='line-break'> </span> very little but I am glad <span class='line-break'> </span> it is gone.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Josie has bin a bout as usual<span class='line-break'> </span> to day.  Betty the (col) girl<span class='line-break'> </span> washed some this morning<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; ironed some this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I fixed some land and<span class='line-break'> </span> planted some onions.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Henry has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> hunting.  Mabel has bin <span class='line-break'> </span> sweet today.  She has staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at the cook room most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2196">
<h3><a name="page-2196">Saturday, October 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='line-break'> </span> A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> some corn &amp; loaded in a <span class='line-break'> </span> cureing of tobacco.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Car went to Mr Powers<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  She got Mr Walters<span class='line-break'> </span> to come and get her &amp; bring<span class='line-break'> </span> her back.  I would be<span class='line-break'> </span> glad that I had money so<span class='line-break'> </span> that I could do something<span class='line-break'> </span> that I want to do. As I am<span class='line-break'> </span> I work and wory to keep<span class='line-break'> </span> things going here and if they<span class='line-break'> </span> take me any where there <span class='line-break'> </span> is so much complaint<span class='line-break'> </span> a bout it I wish I could <span class='line-break'> </span> not want to go any<span class='line-break'> </span> where.  The children has <span class='line-break'> </span> played and fussed all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Julia Fergerson come to see Josie today<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2197">
<h3><a name="page-2197">Sunday, October 29, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  We all eat dinner <span class='line-break'> </span> at home.  Hinny &amp; Edna <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Strait Stone to <span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday School.  Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> started to Gretna with a load<span class='line-break'> </span> of tobacco.  Less [Ro...k?]&amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> his wife &amp; baby &amp; Elsie East<span class='line-break'> </span> come a few minutes.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> went with them.  Was going <span class='line-break'> </span> to Chatham to night.  Lee<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Oscar come a few minutes<span class='line-break'> </span> for Nellie's hand pocket that<span class='line-break'> </span> she forgot.  Mr Steven Davis<span class='line-break'> </span> and his wife &amp; Robert Mayhew<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie today.  Mollie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Johnson come &amp; brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie a nice box of some things<span class='line-break'> </span> to eat. Elsie brought grapes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Alice Thomson brought her a box of candy.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2198">
<h3><a name="page-2198">Monday, October 30, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben worked on <span class='line-break'> </span> his tobacco all day.  Henry and<span class='line-break'> </span> I helped him  finish tieing. <span class='line-break'> </span> Tonight Henry went to Dr.<span class='line-break'> </span> Owens for tablets for his <span class='line-break'> </span> mother.  Jim &amp; Nellie has not <span class='line-break'> </span> come home yet.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school today,  Bettie<span class='line-break'> </span> and I got dinner.  Bettie <span class='line-break'> </span> picked up the walnuts today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel and I went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> barn this evening.  I tied<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco and Mabel played.<span class='line-break'> </span> Etta Gilbert brought<span class='line-break'> </span> me a few dried apples.</p>
