<br />
<div id="page-2199">
<h3><a name="page-2199">Tuesday, October 31, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna.  Ben went<span class='line-break'> </span> for medicine for Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Ben carried some <span class='line-break'> </span> corn to the mill and let<span class='line-break'> </span> me go with him.  I fished<span class='line-break'> </span> while they ground the corn.<span class='line-break'> </span> I caught two fish.  I put<span class='line-break'> </span> them in the branch clack.<span class='line-break'> </span> Sent Josie a bird for her<span class='line-break'> </span> supper.  She eat the bird<span class='line-break'> </span> and then had the head<span class='line-break'> </span> ache.  Fannie went to Mount<span class='line-break'> </span> Ainy[?] to a party.  Halawene<span class='line-break'> </span> they called it.  Mrs Anderson &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Hendricks sent Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> some nice flowers today.<span class='line-break'> </span> She has had a lot of nice <span class='line-break'> </span> flowers sent her.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2200">
<h3><a name="page-2200">Wednesday, November  1, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim stripped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  Jim &amp; Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> went to the barn tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Mr Edmons.  <span class='line-break'> </span> They have a cow choked<span class='line-break'> </span> with a sweet potatoe.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> hope she may get it out and<span class='line-break'> </span> not die.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Mrs George<span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson &amp; Mrs Charley<span class='line-break'> </span> Anderson &amp; Nellie Hendricks<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie.  Nettie<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Josie some grapes.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Booker &amp; little Carol<span class='line-break'> </span> come.  Mr Booker brought<span class='line-break'> </span> pears.  I tied my calf<span class='line-break'> </span> but today she broke her <span class='line-break'> </span> collar and had to be put <span class='line-break'> </span> in a gain. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2201">
<h3><a name="page-2201">Thursday, November  2, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  Nellie helped<span class='line-break'> </span> tie.  Bettie ironed some today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got most of the dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Bettie d[r]essed a chicken for <span class='line-break'> </span> me.  I churned.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Henry  come<span class='line-break'> </span> by Lees and got some <span class='line-break'> </span> beef.  He got to ride most<span class='line-break'> </span> of the way.  Mollie Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie today.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Last night one of Mr <span class='line-break'> </span> Edmons cows got choked <span class='line-break'> </span> with a sweet potatoe.  Lee &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> went down there.  They <span class='line-break'> </span> cut in to her swallow and <span class='line-break'> </span> got out the potatoe.  The cow<span class='line-break'> </span> is getting on Ok they hope.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel is trying her self tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2202">
<h3><a name="page-2202">Friday, November  3, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim finished<span class='line-break'> </span> stripping Bens cureing of <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Ben &amp; Henry and<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie went to Kate Harveys<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Jim tied my calf <span class='line-break'> </span> for me today.  Denia <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Hattie Gilbert<span class='line-break'> </span> washed here today.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Alcie Collans made <span class='line-break'> </span> some soap today.  Bettie<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  We had <span class='line-break'> </span> some nice beef.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> caught a rabbit in his<span class='line-break'> </span> trap this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie finished Carries<span class='line-break'> </span> babys cloak today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2203">
<h3><a name="page-2203">Saturday, November  4, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day cloudy part <span class='line-break'> </span> of the day.  Jim stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco this morning.  Nellie tied.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry went to Kates<span class='line-break'> </span> and got some tobacco and <span class='line-break'> </span> put it in the pit.  Jim come<span class='line-break'> </span> but would not stay and eat<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Thsi evening Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> carried Betty part of the <span class='line-break'> </span> way home.  I went as far <span class='line-break'> </span> as Cedar Forest.  I fished<span class='line-break'> </span> some.  Caught three small<span class='line-break'> </span> fish.  Mr Power sent <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie some birds ready <span class='line-break'> </span> to cook.  I am glad of<span class='line-break'> </span> them to give her.  Fanny<span class='line-break'> </span> Power has gone to Mrs Grave..<span class='line-break'> </span> to night.  Mr Orval Gravely[?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come for her.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2204">
<h3><a name="page-2204">Sunday, November  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day cloudy but no <span class='line-break'> </span> rain.  We all was at home <span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner.  Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Johnson Reynols this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie &amp; I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had nice beef to cook.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has not suffered<span class='line-break'> </span> as bad as usual. Today<span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Power went to<span class='line-break'> </span> church &amp; home.  I hope <span class='line-break'> </span> she is coming back to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Jim &amp; Ben &amp; Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> is at the barn loading<span class='line-break'> </span> the waggon with <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  They want to <span class='line-break'> </span> start to Grena in the<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  I hope they<span class='line-break'> </span> may get off Ok.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p>   </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2205">
<h3><a name="page-2205">Monday, November  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  Nellie churned <span class='line-break'> </span> and washed the dishes for<span class='line-break'> </span> me.  I got the dinner.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Henry started to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna before day this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  They got home a <span class='line-break'> </span> little before night.  Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> was very well pleased<span class='line-break'> </span> with the sale of his<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  He solde a little <span class='line-break'> </span> for Kate.  Mr Lewis<span class='line-break'> </span> brought Josie some good<span class='line-break'> </span> apples this evening.  Mrs Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> sent her some light<span class='line-break'> </span> bread &amp; cake and some<span class='line-break'> </span> beautiful flowers.  Fanny<span class='line-break'> </span> brought them last night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna &amp; Franklin went to school.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2206">
<h3><a name="page-2206">Tuesday, November  7, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day and a little <span class='line-break'> </span> rain.  Ben went to the <span class='line-break'> </span> Election and served as judge.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Nellie stripped <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  John Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> bull got in and got to the <span class='line-break'> </span> haystacks. Did not do any <span class='line-break'> </span> damage.  Our cows got in <span class='line-break'> </span> Norman Bookers field.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim got them out and <span class='line-break'> </span> fixed the fence.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> I hulled walnuts.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel stayed with me<span class='line-break'> </span> at the shop.  I did not<span class='line-break'> </span> go to vote.  I had no way<span class='line-break'> </span> to go.  Several ladies did <span class='line-break'> </span> vote.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2207">
<h3><a name="page-2207">Wednesday, November  8, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day some cooler than<span class='line-break'> </span> yesterdy.  Ben disked some <span class='line-break'> </span> land to sowingness.  Jim &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie stripped tobacco.  It was <span class='line-break'> </span> not in good order.  Mollie<span class='line-break'> </span> come down here a while<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  She would not<span class='line-break'> </span> stay for dinner. I went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Renan this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nat Wooding carried me<span class='line-break'> </span> most of the way over there.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> walked home.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Josie has suffered a lot today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Nel churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> I started Carrie a letter <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Nellie got a letter <span class='line-break'> </span> from Evylin to day.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> glad.  She wanted to hear so bad.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2208">
<h3><a name="page-2208">Thursday, November  9, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> helped me this morning.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> milked two cows and one<span class='line-break'> </span> was not up.  I hunted for <span class='line-break'> </span> her but did not find her.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim found her in Mr Bookers<span class='line-break'> </span> field.  Josie has suffered<span class='line-break'> </span> a lot today.  Mr Irvin Lewis<span class='line-break'> </span> sent Josie a nice box of<span class='line-break'> </span> grapes by mail today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Dews come tonight<span class='line-break'> </span> and paid Mrs Car some<span class='line-break'> </span> mony.  Fannie Power and <span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed some this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am so glad that it is done.<span class='line-break'> </span> I s[t]arched some clothes<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2209">
<h3><a name="page-2209">Friday, November 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear cool day. Mr Kent<span class='line-break'> </span> come tonight.  She brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie some [oiters?].  I am glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that she did.  They will be <span class='line-break'> </span> something that she has not had<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Nellie worked on their<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco all day.  I ironed <span class='line-break'> </span> some &amp; Fanny ironed some <span class='line-break'> </span> so we got all the things done.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to the ball game.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got a letter from Carrie.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad.  Jim got a letter <span class='line-break'> </span> from John.  I was glad <span class='line-break'> </span> to hear from him.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2210">
<h3><a name="page-2210">Saturday, November 11, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Ben loaded on Kate's <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco this evening.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Booker and Ruth Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jessie Power come to see <span class='line-break'> </span> her today.  Norman Booker <span class='line-break'> </span> killed a calf this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben helped him and got a <span class='line-break'> </span> part of the calf.  Fannie<span class='line-break'> </span> Power went to Gretna this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  She went with Jamie<span class='line-break'> </span> Gravely &amp; her [beau?].  Ruth<span class='line-break'> </span> Booker brought some<span class='line-break'> </span> apples this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner. <div id="page-2211">
<h3><a name="page-2211">Sunday, November 12, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Mr Sam <span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbard come for them while<span class='line-break'> </span> we were at dinner.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Marvin and all the children<span class='line-break'> </span> except Reese Henry went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday School.  Mr Anderson<span class='line-break'> </span> come for Miss Fannie Power<span class='line-break'> </span> and carried her to church.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim &amp; Henry has<span class='line-break'> </span> gone to load some tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie tried to persuade<span class='line-break'> </span> then to wait until morning<span class='line-break'> </span> but I think it suited<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim best to load tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> I am glad that Josie's sisters<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see her.  Want them <span class='line-break'> </span> to come every time they can.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2212">
<h3><a name="page-2212">Monday, November 13, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> corn all day.  Jim went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna with tobacco.  He <span class='line-break'> </span> has not come home yet.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie got a present from<span class='line-break'> </span> Evylin today.  A work bag.<span class='line-break'> </span> Virginia Harvey spent the day<span class='line-break'> </span> here with Fannie Power.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad that she come.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hettie washed here today. I <span class='line-break'> </span> churned &amp; and got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I wanted to go to the mill<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; fish a while &amp; get some<span class='line-break'> </span> [brand] but Ben talked so<span class='line-break'> </span> belittling a bout it.  Would <span class='line-break'> </span> not go.  I am not as good<span class='line-break'> </span> as a servant should be. <span class='line-break'> </span> Ben dont know how much I wait on him and his crowd.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2213">
<h3><a name="page-2213">Tuesday, November 14, 1922</a></h3>

He carried wheat<span class='line-break'> </span> did not get it ground. He brought<span class='line-break'> </span> 1000 weight of brand.  Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with him.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie milked the cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie got supper. Nellie is<span class='line-break'> </span> busy making a dress for a <span class='line-break'> </span> little girl in Charlottesville.<span class='line-break'> </span> Some one sent Josie a box<span class='line-break'> </span> of flowers by mail today. <span class='line-break'> </span> Mollie Reynols come today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I would of bin glad to see her.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

This <span class='line-break'> </span> evening they could not do<span class='line-break'> </span> much of any thing. I finished <span class='line-break'> </span> hulling walnuts.  <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Hattie finished getting out<span class='line-break'> </span> peas and we divided them.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Launa Davis (col) come<span class='line-break'> </span> here for some [...?] for<span class='line-break'> </span> her sick son.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Nellie sowed.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie ironed some this <span class='line-break'> </span> morning. They <span class='line-break'> </span> will have a mudy walke.<span class='line-break'> </span> The wind is bowing to night.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2215">
<h3><a name="page-2215">Thursday, November 16, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> corn all the morning.  This evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Gretna.  Fanny [..?]<span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with him.  He <span class='line-break'> </span> had a puncture.  Stuck a nail <span class='line-break'> </span> through his tire.  He had good <span class='line-break'> </span> luck mending it. We made <span class='line-break'> </span> the trip ok.  I bought a few<span class='line-break'> </span> thing.  Among them a sweater <span class='line-break'> </span> for Edna.  Jim went to Mr Steven [Dais's?].<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner &amp; churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school.  Josie did not suffer<span class='line-break'> </span> very much today.  No one <span class='line-break'> </span> come to see her today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mabel staid with Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  She has bin <span class='line-break'> </span> happy with her waggon today.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2216">
<h3><a name="page-2216">Friday, November 17, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  The boys hauled up<span class='line-break'> </span> stalks and corn.  Very glad they <span class='line-break'> </span> have got as much as they have.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie sewed some.  She washed <span class='line-break'> </span> the dishes and fixed the milk<span class='line-break'> </span> ready to churn.  Fannie ironed.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  We had cabbage.<span class='line-break'> </span> They were a rarity.  Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered a lot today.  Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Lewis sent her some <span class='line-break'> </span> nice fruit this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> The people send her some <span class='line-break'> </span> thing nearly every day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie has started to [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Gladis to a school<span class='line-break'> </span> entertainment. George Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> come for her.  I want to <span class='line-break'> </span> see all of my children<span class='line-break'> </span> so bad but cant.</p>

<div id="page-2217">
<h3><a name="page-2217">Saturday, November 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>[note at top of page] I turned two leaves and wrote on<span class='line-break'> </span> the wrong page.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> A cloudy day and a little rain.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Jim and Henry cut stalks<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. This evening Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> was caught by the band and<span class='line-break'> </span> had his shirt and pants torn<span class='line-break'> </span> off of him. It is a wonder that <span class='line-break'> </span> he was not kill. He was not<span class='line-break'> </span> hurt much. Broke his watch<span class='line-break'> </span> all to pieces. Mrs. Booker and<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Kelie come to see Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening. Mr. Kellie come<span class='line-break'> </span> for them. Mrs Rufus Carr<span class='line-break'> </span> sent Josie some birds. Ben and<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Henry went to Strait<span class='line-break'> </span> Stone for some barrels. They<span class='line-break'> </span> got them. Fannie went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Kates this evening to spend<span class='line-break'> </span> the night. Hattie cleaned the yard<span class='line-break'> </span> some this morning.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-2218">
<h3><a name="page-2218">Sunday, November 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Part of a wild<span class='line-break'> </span> turkey. Several other things.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey and Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> Fergerson come a little<span class='line-break'> </span> while. Mr. Tom Wooding<span class='line-break'> </span> died today. They sent for<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim and Ben. They had<span class='line-break'> </span> company and did not<span class='line-break'> </span> go until late. Ben is there <span class='line-break'> </span> now. Nellie and I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner. Josie has not<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered so much <span class='line-break'> </span> today. I feel worried about<span class='line-break'> </span> every thing. Got the blues I guess.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2220">
<h3><a name="page-2220">Tuesday, November 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

Fletcher Car <span class='line-break'> </span> carried the children to school<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. Have just got back<span class='line-break'> </span> here tonight.  Nellie has helped<span class='line-break'> </span> me and sewed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim got the Turkey<span class='line-break'> </span> in the hen house tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna said she would tell<span class='line-break'> </span> me something to write.  She<span class='line-break'> </span> said that Alice Massa was <span class='line-break'> </span> married last Sat.<span class='line-break'> </span> Johnson Reynols &amp; wife<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Chatham today .  I could <span class='line-break'> </span> of went but was crowded out  <span class='line-break'> </span> by company. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-2221">
<h3><a name="page-2221">Wednesday, November 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very windy.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> cut wood until dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Then they killed 15 turkey.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie &amp; I helped tp pick<span class='line-break'> </span> them.  Denia Blair come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fletcher Car &amp; his mother <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; wife went to Mr Dews<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Mr Powers this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Lelia Car &amp; Nellie <span class='line-break'> </span> got supper &amp; washed <span class='line-break'> </span> dishes to night.  I did<span class='line-break'> </span> not milk tonight. It was<span class='line-break'> </span> was late when we come from <span class='line-break'> </span> the spring.  We had a <span class='line-break'> </span> big frost.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Lelia<span class='line-break'> </span> Car ironed some this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.</p>

</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2222">
<h3><a name="page-2222">Thursday, November 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna this morning &amp; Nel<span class='line-break'> </span> went with him.  He carried<span class='line-break'> </span> the turkeys that we picked<span class='line-break'> </span> yesterday.  Got home by ten <span class='line-break'> </span> oclock.  Nel got most of the<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I churned.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> cut wood in the woods.  Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled wood this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> This morning Mr Fletcher<span class='line-break'> </span> Car &amp; Mrs Car &amp; Fanny<span class='line-break'> </span> Power went to Jim Powers<span class='line-break'> </span> and spent the day.  Got<span class='line-break'> </span> back about dark.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> got supper tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben has gone to<span class='line-break'> </span> Renan to help Irvin<span class='line-break'> </span> Harvey load on some tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope he may do well[with it?].</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2223">
<h3><a name="page-2223">Friday, November 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> hauled wood.  They had <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Bookers team.  Irvin Harvey<span class='line-break'> </span> had our horses and went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna with tobacco.  Mr<span class='line-break'> </span> Fletcher Car went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Chatham.  His mother wife <span class='line-break'> </span> and I went with him.<span class='line-break'> </span> We had a good trip.  Come<span class='line-break'> </span> home for dinner.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner and churned. <span class='line-break'> </span> Carrie &amp; Marvin and<span class='line-break'> </span> three of the children<span class='line-break'> </span> come a little while.  I was<span class='line-break'> </span> very glad to see them.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Denia Blair &amp; Sallie<span class='line-break'> </span> come by here going to<span class='line-break'> </span> see Mrs Trent.  I would<span class='line-break'> </span> of bin glad to see them.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2224">
<h3><a name="page-2224">Saturday, November 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde windy day. Jim <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Ben hauled wood this morning <span class='line-break'> </span> and sawed wood all evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr &amp; Mrs. Carr left home <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning for Long Island <span class='line-break'> </span> and then they would <span class='line-break'> </span> start for Home at Jewel <span class='line-break'> </span> Ridge Va. I certainly did <span class='line-break'> </span> enjoy their stay here.  Mollie <span class='line-break'> </span> and Robert Reynols come <span class='line-break'> </span> a few minutes this morning.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Robert is looking well.<span class='line-break'> </span> I was glad that they come<span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie Gilbent washed <span class='line-break'> </span> a little here this morning. <span class='line-break'> </span> Tonight is very colde. The <span class='line-break'> </span> coldest of this fall. <span class='line-break'> </span> Oh how I do dread the <span class='line-break'> </span> winter but it will soon be well over.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2225">
<h3><a name="page-2225">Sunday, November 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear colde day.  We all eat <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner at home today.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Sunday School this <span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Nellie baked a cake <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  I fried beef<span class='line-break'> </span> steak.  Fannie stewed oisters<span class='line-break'> </span> and I thought we had a <span class='line-break'> </span> nice dinnner. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Lee &amp; Grace Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> come to Mr Norman Bookers<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  Grace &amp; Ruth<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Grace brought<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie some beautiful<span class='line-break'> </span> flowers.  Josie has felt mighty<span class='line-break'> </span> bad all day today.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2226">
<h3><a name="page-2226">Monday, November 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>This morning it was snowing.  <span class='line-break'> </span> The first snow of this winter.<span class='line-break'> </span> It has bin cloudy all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben put some <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco in the pit &amp; helped<span class='line-break'> </span> Norman Booker get some down <span class='line-break'> </span> on the ground tier.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie home.  I hope she<span class='line-break'> </span> wont stay long at home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie &amp; her Grandma need<span class='line-break'> </span> her so bad.  Ben heard<span class='line-break'> </span> from the turkeys.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> solde well.  Edna come<span class='line-break'> </span> home with the head ache<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; sore throat.  I hope she<span class='line-break'> </span> will not be sick.  Mabel<span class='line-break'> </span> cut off the dolles hair <span class='line-break'> </span> today.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2227">
<h3><a name="page-2227">Tuesday, November 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde day for Nov.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim worked on <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco some today.  It was<span class='line-break'> </span> two dry so they could not<span class='line-break'> </span> do much with it.  Hattie<span class='line-break'> </span> washed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> sewed some.  Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> felt very bad today.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school.  Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Renan for stove pipe.<span class='line-break'> </span> Could not get it.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim had a letter from <span class='line-break'> </span> John today.  Nellie heard<span class='line-break'> </span> from Evylin to day.<span class='line-break'> </span> I killed &amp; dressed a <span class='line-break'> </span> turkey.  Want to cook it<span class='line-break'> </span> for Thanksgiving.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2228">
<h3><a name="page-2228">Wednesday, November 29, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped a little tobacco this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  This evening they <span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna.  Ben went<span class='line-break'> </span> for Fanny today.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> washed the dishes &amp; churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> Then she sewed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate Harvey come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie to day.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Will <span class='line-break'> </span> not go any more until <span class='line-break'> </span> Monday.  Several of the <span class='line-break'> </span> neighbors killed hogs today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has not suffered <span class='line-break'> </span> so much today as she <span class='line-break'> </span> did yesterday.  Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Jim went to the barns<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight to tie tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2229">
<h3><a name="page-2229">Thursday, November 30, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear good day.  Jim &amp; Ben stripped tobacco all <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  Henry and Edna went<span class='line-break'> </span> to Mr George Eemersons to <span class='line-break'> </span> a birth day party.  Lawsons birth<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  They had a fine time.  Julia<span class='line-break'> </span> Emerson come with them home.<span class='line-break'> </span> Cordie Blair come to see<span class='line-break'> </span> Aunt Jo this evening.  Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> has suffered awful this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Heard today that <span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Rufus Car got his finger<span class='line-break'> </span> cut very bad sawing wood.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got dinner.  Had a turkey<span class='line-break'> </span> for dinner.  We all enjoyed<span class='line-break'> </span> it very much. Fannie thought<span class='line-break'> </span> Hellen was comeing to<span class='line-break'> </span> stay until bed time.<span class='line-break'> </span> Billie Emerson &amp; Henry &amp; B &amp; Lawson Emerson has gone hunting.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Thanksgiving Day.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2230">
<h3><a name="page-2230">Friday, December  1, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim worked<span class='line-break'> </span> at the barn most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> They helped Norman Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> cut feed a little while.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ruth &amp; Lottie Booker &amp; [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> come a while.  Lizzie Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> come this evening.  Mr Bennett<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Earl come by for her<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  I was glad she come<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Hubbard sent<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie a nice box of good<span class='line-break'> </span> things to eat by mail.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie washed some for<span class='line-break'> </span> her self this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie ironed some this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Josie has not<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered so bad today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Julia Emerson went from <span class='line-break'> </span> here this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2231">
<h3><a name="page-2231">Saturday, December  2, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim &amp; Ben <span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  Henry shucked<span class='line-break'> </span> a littl corn.  Elie &amp; Lewis [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> shucked one shock and got<span class='line-break'> </span> up the corn &amp; stalks. <span class='line-break'> </span> Elie went to the store for<span class='line-break'> </span> me.  Fanny Power went to <span class='line-break'> </span> George Blairs tonight. They<span class='line-break'> </span> have a lot of young <span class='line-break'> </span> company there tonight.  The<span class='line-break'> </span> Bennetts come down this evening<span class='line-break'> </span> Lizzie sent me a nice<span class='line-break'> </span> peice of beef.  I am so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> of it.  Glad to be remembered.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a letter from Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  I was so glad to <span class='line-break'> </span> hear from her.  Wish I could <span class='line-break'> </span> see them all.  Mollie<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this evening.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2232">
<h3><a name="page-2232">Sunday, December  3, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  We were all at <span class='line-break'> </span> home at dinner.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Sunday School.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben &amp; Jim and<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to Lees.  I sent<span class='line-break'> </span> some butter. Hellen will sell <span class='line-break'> </span> it at Altavista.  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Roasted two chickens.<span class='line-break'> </span> Late this evening Carrie &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Kate and Reese &amp; [Juilia?]<span class='line-break'> </span> was with them come.  Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> eat dinner with Kate.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> wish I could of bin with <span class='line-break'> </span> them.  Dr Wigginton &amp; Pearl <span class='line-break'> </span> was at Kates.  Hattie gil[Gilbert?]<span class='line-break'> </span> col)[coloured girl]come &amp; helped to<span class='line-break'> </span> straiten up things this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  Edna &amp; Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Mabel has gone to bed.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2233">
<h3><a name="page-2233">Monday, December  4, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A raining tonight.  The boys<span class='line-break'> </span> finished stripping Bens cureing<span class='line-break'> </span> of tobacco and put some of <span class='line-break'> </span> Jims in the pit.  The children<span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Nellie &amp; I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Hattie Gilbert washed<span class='line-break'> </span> and all of the clothes is on the <span class='line-break'> </span> garden fence.  Josie has suffered<span class='line-break'> </span> a lot today.  Nellie heard<span class='line-break'> </span> from Evylin today.  I planted<span class='line-break'> </span> a few little bulbs today.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben and Norman Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> wanted to start to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> in the morning but they<span class='line-break'> </span> could not load their <span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco so they cant go.<span class='line-break'> </span> Our cows got in Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> field this morning.  Jim got them<span class='line-break'> </span> out.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2234">
<h3><a name="page-2234">Tuesday, December  5, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Mr Booker<span class='line-break'> </span> put their tobacco on the waggon<span class='line-break'> </span> and started to Gretna a bout<span class='line-break'> </span> 10 oclock.  Nellie &amp; Henry has <span class='line-break'> </span> gone to Mr Bookers to stay<span class='line-break'> </span> until he comes home.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> is tying tobacco by him<span class='line-break'> </span> self.  Nellie tied tobacco this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  I got dinner.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> sewed a little this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> I starched the clothes.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Mabel and I <span class='line-break'> </span> [shelled?] some corn.  This <span class='line-break'> </span> evening I started a letter<span class='line-break'> </span> to Effie Brumfield.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jamie Gravely stopped<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Josie this morning.<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna got a letter from<span class='line-break'> </span> Virginia Wooding today.<span class='line-break'> </span>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2235">
<h3><a name="page-2235">Wednesday, December  6, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Jim stripped<span class='line-break'> </span> tobacco.  Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car to Long Island.<span class='line-break'> </span> She intends going to Lynchley[?].<span class='line-break'> </span> I hope she may keep well <span class='line-break'> </span> and come back soon.  Fanny<span class='line-break'> </span> is taking care of Josie.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie sent a box to<span class='line-break'> </span> Evylin today.  I got a <span class='line-break'> </span> snack to eat for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I ironed most of the <span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Denia Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> sent Mabel some papers <span class='line-break'> </span> to cut up and a bag <span class='line-break'> </span> of rags that Mrs Anderson<span class='line-break'> </span> sent for Josie.  Henry<span class='line-break'> </span> caught a rabbit this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  I was glad of<span class='line-break'> </span> it.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2236">
<h3><a name="page-2236">Thursday, December  7, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> stripped tobacco.  The children <span class='line-break'> </span> went to school.  Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to a ball game at [...ting?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Went with Lawson Emerson.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie ironed some this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning.  I ironed this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Finished what was to do.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie &amp; I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> I milked tonight &amp; Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Edna got supper.  Nel<span class='line-break'> </span> let Edna make the bread<span class='line-break'> </span> for supper.  It was good.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fannie has bin with<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie all day.  Mrs Car<span class='line-break'> </span> has not come yet.  Guess <span class='line-break'> </span> it will be a day or<span class='line-break'> </span> two yet before she comes.<span class='line-break'> </span> We will be glad when she comes.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2237">
<h3><a name="page-2237">Friday, December  8, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on the tobacco most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening Ben went to <span class='line-break'> </span> the island to meet Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Car.  She had come from <span class='line-break'> </span> [Lynchburg?].  Mabel and <span class='line-break'> </span> I went with him.  We<span class='line-break'> </span> staid at Peaks store while<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben went to Mr Cars<span class='line-break'> </span> for Mrs Car.  I went <span class='line-break'> </span> to see Mrs Hutcherson<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  She is very<span class='line-break'> </span> sick.  She had a lot of <span class='line-break'> </span> company.  Mr Walter<span class='line-break'> </span> Car sent Josie a big fish<span class='line-break'> </span> by mail this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> She eat some of it for<span class='line-break'> </span> supper.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2238">
<h3><a name="page-2238">Saturday, December  9, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A bad day.  Rained some.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim stripped tobacco<span class='line-break'> </span> all day and are tying<span class='line-break'> </span> tonight.  Nellie cleaned my<span class='line-break'> </span> suit today.  I am glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> she did.  Fanny has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Doris Brumfield to <span class='line-break'> </span> night.  Nellie and I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  Edna &amp; Franklin<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Mr Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Mrs Mayhew<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; [Audna?] passed here today.<span class='line-break'> </span> They had bin to see Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Hutcherson.  Johnson Reynols<span class='line-break'> </span> come here today looking <span class='line-break'> </span> for his dog.  They hunted<span class='line-break'> </span> some down here yesterday.<span class='line-break'> </span> He brought Josie two birds.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2239">
<h3><a name="page-2239">Sunday, December 10, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Very colde tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> We was all at home at dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to Sunday School.<span class='line-break'> </span> This evening I went to Reynols.<span class='line-break'> </span> I started walking.  Jo Edmons <span class='line-break'> </span> overtook me at the bridge<span class='line-break'> </span> and ask me to ride.  He carried<span class='line-break'> </span> me to the sand clay road.<span class='line-break'> </span> I walked the rest of the way.<span class='line-break'> </span> Johnson brought me home.<span class='line-break'> </span> I had a good visit.  Posie &amp; Kate<span class='line-break'> </span> was there.  Nellie &amp; I got <span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I cooked a chicken.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie baked a cake.  It was <span class='line-break'> </span> fine.  [Ren?] &amp; Ethel Worsham<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> sorrie not to have seen <span class='line-break'> </span> them.  Hope they will come<span class='line-break'> </span> a gain soon.  Good night.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2240">
<h3><a name="page-2240">Monday, December 11, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde cloudy day.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> and Mr Booker and Claud <span class='line-break'> </span> Edmons &amp; a darkey killed our<span class='line-break'> </span> hogs &amp; Mr Bookers.  Ellen <span class='line-break'> </span> Lewis &amp; Hattie Gilbert helped.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ellen helped Mrs Booker.  We got<span class='line-break'> </span> on fine.  Did not try to work <span class='line-break'> </span> on the meat tonight.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  She cooked birds<span class='line-break'> </span> and a rabbit.  We had pork <span class='line-break'> </span> for supper.  I got a letter<span class='line-break'> </span> from Carrie today.  I am always<span class='line-break'> </span> so glad to hear from them.<span class='line-break'> </span> Wish I could go up there<span class='line-break'> </span> once more.  Mrs Car gave <span class='line-break'> </span> me a peice of goods to make<span class='line-break'> </span> me a dress.  I think it is <span class='line-break'> </span> pretty.  That is a Xmas gift.<span class='line-break'> </span> Wish it was made.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2241">
<h3><a name="page-2241">Tuesday, December 12, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim &amp; Ben finished stripping<span class='line-break'> </span> Jims cureing of tobacco and<span class='line-break'> </span> loaded it on the waggon ready<span class='line-break'> </span> for market.  They have gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to Renan tonight.  Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> suffered a lot today.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> and Fanny ground the <span class='line-break'> </span> sausage meat and made the <span class='line-break'> </span> sausage.  That was a great<span class='line-break'> </span> help.  I dried out the [?].<span class='line-break'> </span> Worked at the wash house <span class='line-break'> </span> all the evening.  I am so <span class='line-break'> </span> glad that much is done.<span class='line-break'> </span> The children went to <span class='line-break'> </span> school.  Franklin come<span class='line-break'> </span> home complaining but he <span class='line-break'> </span> is Ok now as far as I can <span class='line-break'> </span> tell.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2242">
<h3><a name="page-2242">Wednesday, December 13, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy cold day.  Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> went to Gretna with tobacco.<span class='line-break'> </span> Started before day.  Did not <span class='line-break'> </span> sell.  He came home &amp; brought<span class='line-break'> </span> the team.  Ben got Mr <span class='line-break'> </span> Bookers team and went to <span class='line-break'> </span> the mill.  I am so glad<span class='line-break'> </span> that he did go as we was<span class='line-break'> </span> out of flour &amp; cornmeal.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has bin pent all day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny &amp; Mrs Car has worked<span class='line-break'> </span> on Mrs Cars dress some<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  Nellie &amp; I got dinner. <span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie Gilbert(col) washed<span class='line-break'> </span> here today.  Henry turned<span class='line-break'> </span> over a churn of milk<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning be for he<span class='line-break'> </span> started to school.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2243">
<h3><a name="page-2243">Thursday, December 14, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very bad day colde and raining.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim went to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> with [Thellbert?] Edmons.<span class='line-break'> </span> He solde his tobacco and <span class='line-break'> </span> got home before night.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben helped Mr Edmons<span class='line-break'> </span> kill his hogs today.  Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner &amp; churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> I cleaned the hogs <span class='line-break'> </span> heads &amp; feet.  I am very <span class='line-break'> </span> glad that is done.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car sewed on her <span class='line-break'> </span> dress to day.  Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> bin quiet today.  The <span class='line-break'> </span> children went to school.<span class='line-break'> </span> They are talking tonight<span class='line-break'> </span> so that you cant hear<span class='line-break'> </span> no one but them.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2244">
<h3><a name="page-2244">Friday, December 15, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A bad day.  Rained most all<span class='line-break'> </span> day.  The children went <span class='line-break'> </span> to school.  Ben &amp; Jim did not<span class='line-break'> </span> do much of anything. Nellie<span class='line-break'> </span> ironed some.  I got dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> except make the bread.  I <span class='line-break'> </span> boiled meat &amp; made<span class='line-break'> </span> scrapple.  Jim carried the <span class='line-break'> </span> things home that we had <span class='line-break'> </span> borrowed.  I am glad that <span class='line-break'> </span> is done.  Josie got Ednas &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Mabels dresses that she had<span class='line-break'> </span> ordered.  They are very pretty.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben bought goods to make<span class='line-break'> </span> Edna some gowns.  I have<span class='line-break'> </span> rocked little Mabel to sleep<span class='line-break'> </span> and put her in bed.  she is <span class='line-break'> </span> so petted that she dont know<span class='line-break'> </span> what to do with her self.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2245">
<h3><a name="page-2245">Saturday, December 16, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy bad day.  No rain <span class='line-break'> </span> to hinder work.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood for Mr Booker.<span class='line-break'> </span> They eat dinner there.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben said he did enjoy the <span class='line-break'> </span> beans.  I cooked some big <span class='line-break'> </span> sweet potatoes.  Boiled hogs <span class='line-break'> </span> feet.  The children got in<span class='line-break'> </span> some wood.  Henry went<span class='line-break'> </span> to the store &amp; got a can <span class='line-break'> </span> of oil.  Heard today that <span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Hurcherson is very<span class='line-break'> </span> sick.  Also heard that Mrs <span class='line-break'> </span> Compton &amp; Mr Compton<span class='line-break'> </span> are sick.  I hope they all <span class='line-break'> </span> may be better soon.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim hunted just<span class='line-break'> </span> at night.  Ben killed one<span class='line-break'> </span> rabbit.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p>  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2246">
<h3><a name="page-2246">Sunday, December 17, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A very bad day.  We all staid<span class='line-break'> </span> at home all day.  Nellie &amp; I<span class='line-break'> </span> got dinner.  Nel baked potato<span class='line-break'> </span> pies.  I cooked cabbage &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> back bones.  Nellie churned.<span class='line-break'> </span> I fixed up the butter.<span class='line-break'> </span> Johnson come here a while.<span class='line-break'> </span> He was talkeing a bout<span class='line-break'> </span> fixing for Xmas.  I done <span class='line-break'> </span> want to fix much but <span class='line-break'> </span> will do the best I can.<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim went to John<span class='line-break'> </span> Hubbards he said <span class='line-break'> </span> to see about getting<span class='line-break'> </span> a goat.  He said it was <span class='line-break'> </span> dead.  I did not want it<span class='line-break'> </span> here any way.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2247">
<h3><a name="page-2247">Monday, December 18, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> shucked some corn.  Hunted<span class='line-break'> </span> a little then went to <span class='line-break'> </span> Strait Stone &amp; home <span class='line-break'> </span> before night.  Nellie made <span class='line-break'> </span> Edna two gowns.  She is <span class='line-break'> </span> sleeping in one tonight.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie washed two hams<span class='line-break'> </span> this evening one for me <span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; one for her self.  I cooked<span class='line-break'> </span> meat &amp; made scrapple <span class='line-break'> </span> this evening.  I boiled<span class='line-break'> </span> the chidlings at the wash<span class='line-break'> </span> house today.  Denia Blair<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see us this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> Carlton Daniels &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> Rufus Car come up here<span class='line-break'> </span> to see Mrs Car this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2248">
<h3><a name="page-2248">Tuesday, December 19, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A clear colde day.  Snowed <span class='line-break'> </span> a little last night.  Jim has<span class='line-break'> </span> bin a round home most of the <span class='line-break'> </span> day.  He put the pea hulls in <span class='line-break'> </span> sacks this morning.  Ben &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Power went to Gretna<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning and to Dunvill<span class='line-break'> </span> on the train.  I got dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie made beds &amp; swept<span class='line-break'> </span> the floors.  Josie has bin <span class='line-break'> </span> quiet most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car has stayed by<span class='line-break'> </span> her most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Hattie Gilbert washed<span class='line-break'> </span> here today.  The clothes did<span class='line-break'> </span> not get dry.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
<p> Ben &amp; Fanny has come home.  <span class='line-break'> </span> The children is so glad.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2249">
<h3><a name="page-2249">Wednesday, December 20, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A cloudy dreary day but no<span class='line-break'> </span> falling weather.  Jim stayed a<span class='line-break'> </span> round home most of the day.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben moved in a hand.  John <span class='line-break'> </span> Ward.  He was until dark <span class='line-break'> </span> getting home.  Then he carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny Power and the children<span class='line-break'> </span> to the school house to a play.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie baked two cakes<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Fanny one and made some<span class='line-break'> </span> pies.  Fanny ironed some/<span class='line-break'> </span> The cloths was not dry<span class='line-break'> </span> eneough to iron good.  I<span class='line-break'> </span> mended Edna's coat this <span class='line-break'> </span> morning &amp; churned and fixed<span class='line-break'> </span> up the butter this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> Josie has suffered bad <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I had a letter from Carrie <span class='line-break'> </span> today.  It is very colde tonight too.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2250">
<h3><a name="page-2250">Thursday, December 21, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A colde clear day.  A little <span class='line-break'> </span> rain last night and a sleet<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Ben went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna.  He carried a barrel <span class='line-break'> </span> of things for Jim to ship<span class='line-break'> </span> to Evylin at Charlottesville.<span class='line-break'> </span> Nellie started to see Evylin <span class='line-break'> </span> this morning.  Ben carried<span class='line-break'> </span> Fanny home this evening.<span class='line-break'> </span> We will miss them very <span class='line-break'> </span> much.  Heard tonight that<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Hutcherson is very sick.<span class='line-break'> </span> Ernest Craddock &amp; family<span class='line-break'> </span> moved to this neighbor hood<span class='line-break'> </span> today.  I hope they will never<span class='line-break'> </span> regret it.  Jim went to<span class='line-break'> </span> Gretna with Ben this evening.  <span class='line-break'> </span> He put up the fence a <span class='line-break'> </span> round the hog lot.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2251">
<h3><a name="page-2251">Friday, December 22, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben &amp; Jim<span class='line-break'> </span> sawed wood for Kate.  I am<span class='line-break'> </span> glad that they did.  I have<span class='line-break'> </span> bin busy all day and done<span class='line-break'> </span> very little.  I got dinner.  Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Car picked the salit yesterday.<span class='line-break'> </span> I got a present of a  nice<span class='line-break'> </span> fruit cake.  Effie Brumfield<span class='line-break'> </span> sent it.  I got a card from<span class='line-break'> </span> Thelma Brumfield.  I am <span class='line-break'> </span> always glad to hear<span class='line-break'> </span> from them.  Jim has gone<span class='line-break'> </span> to Hutchersons to hear<span class='line-break'> </span> from Mrs Hutcherson.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2252">
<h3><a name="page-2252">Saturday, December 23, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  Ben made a dog<span class='line-break'> </span> house &amp; worked on a lounge<span class='line-break'> </span> in the parlor the rest of<span class='line-break'> </span> the day.  I boiled a <span class='line-break'> </span> ham to day.  I got dinner<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; churned.  Washed the <span class='line-break'> </span> babys cap &amp; two cloaks<span class='line-break'> </span> and ironed some.<span class='line-break'> </span> The mail brought <span class='line-break'> </span> several presents for <span class='line-break'> </span> Josie from Miss Bessie<span class='line-break'> </span> Hobson.  Thelma sent<span class='line-break'> </span> things and a box of<span class='line-break'> </span> candy for me.<span class='line-break'> </span> The boys caught a <span class='line-break'> </span> possome to night.  They<span class='line-break'> </span> give it to John Ward.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2253">
<h3><a name="page-2253">Sunday, December 24, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  We were<span class='line-break'> </span> all at home for dinner.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry went to Sunday<span class='line-break'> </span> School &amp; to Johnson <span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols.  No one come to <span class='line-break'> </span> see us today.  Josie has<span class='line-break'> </span> felt bad today.  I got<span class='line-break'> </span> dinner.  I did not go to the<span class='line-break'> </span> spring.  Jim &amp; Henry brought <span class='line-break'> </span> some water.  Etta Gilbert<span class='line-break'> </span> brought 4 buckets full.<span class='line-break'> </span> I dress two chickens.<span class='line-break'> </span> Henry caught a rabbit.<span class='line-break'> </span> He skned that.  Johnson<span class='line-break'> </span> Reynols brought Josie<span class='line-break'> </span> some grapefruit &amp; boiled<span class='line-break'> </span> ham this evening.  Edna<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Franklin brought the <span class='line-break'> </span> water for tonight.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2254">
<h3><a name="page-2254">Monday, December 25, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day.  We were all <span class='line-break'> </span> at home for dinner.  Jim &amp; Ben<span class='line-break'> </span> helped dig Mrs Hutchersons<span class='line-break'> </span> grave.  Marvin &amp; Carrie &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span> all the children come a little<span class='line-break'> </span> while today.  Marvin &amp; Carrie<span class='line-break'> </span> and Reese went to the burial.<span class='line-break'> </span> I did see a lot of people<span class='line-break'> </span> that I knew.  I was glad to <span class='line-break'> </span> seem all.  Would<span class='line-break'> </span> like to go to Johnsons while<span class='line-break'> </span> the children are at home<span class='line-break'> </span> but guess I cant go.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mrs Car got a nice box<span class='line-break'> </span> from Fletcher. Ethel [W...?]<span class='line-break'> </span> gave me a nice box this<span class='line-break'> </span> evening.  Wish I could see<span class='line-break'> </span> all of my folks this Xmas.<span class='line-break'> </span> Guess I cant see many of them.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2255">
<h3><a name="page-2255">Tuesday, December 26, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A beautiful day. The boys hunted some.  We had no company until about night then Bruce Reynolds and his wife &amp; Julia &amp; Mildred Fergerson come a little while. I got dinner and churned then milked the cows. Did not get any supper. George Barber and Earnest Pool had trouble.  Barber drove into Pools buggy. Did not hurt any one much. The horse ran away. I hope they may settle with out a fuss. Henry has gone to Reynols tonight. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2256">
<h3><a name="page-2256">Wednesday, December 27, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good morning again. This evening we were all at home except Henry. He was at Reynols.  This evening Ben and Jim went to Altavista.  Jim wanted to get his teeth pulled.  The dentist was not in town.  They got home about dark.  Jim has gone to Mr. Bookers to hear about Pools and Barbers troubles.  I got dinner and churned and milked morning &amp; evening. Mrs Booker came to see Josie this evening. Went home through the rain.  I fed the horses and hogs for the first time this year and I guess it will be the last. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2257">
<h3><a name="page-2257">Thursday, December 28, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A rainy bad day most of the day. The wind is blowing tonight. Were all at home at dinner except Jim.  I got dinner &amp; churned. Milked morning and evening. Henry went to Mount Amy this morning.  Mrs. Booker and Ethel Wooding and Elsie East come to see Josie a few minutes today. Josie has bin feeling bad today.  I have seen people moveing today.  They had six one horse wagons. The most I had seen in a long time. Dont know who they were that was moveing. They had a bad time for it.  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2258">
<h3><a name="page-2258">Friday, December 29, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day. Jim hunted some today.  Ben made some steps to the house in the wood.  This evening he carried John (the col man) and his family to Cedar Forest.  He got in the mud as he come home and had to prize the car out. Ella Hubbard come this morning and Kate [?] and Lizzie and Lonnie and Alma Bennett. I was glad to see all of them.  We heard today that Cabbel Mattox was killed near Ray. A tractor turned over on him.  Josie is feeling bad tonight.  Oh I am so sorry for her and can't help her in any way.  </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2259">
<h3><a name="page-2259">Saturday, December 30, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>A good day.  I got breakfast. Fried birds and made chicken hash. Ella Hubbard and Lizzie Bennett was here. Lizzie went home before dinner.  Lonnie come for her.  Isla Blair come and brought Josie a box of good things to eat.  It was very nice.  Ella went home right after dinner.  George Hutcherson come for her.  Ben went to see Ken Adkins, he has been very sick but is better now. Henry went to Mr [Milans?] this morning and a boy came home with him that goes to school at Chatham come home with the [Milan?] boy and Floid R.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2260">
<h3><a name="page-2260">Sunday, December 31, 1922</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>365<span class='line-break'> </span> Sunday, Dec. 31, 1922<span class='line-break'> </span> A colde cloudy day - no weather<span class='line-break'> </span> Ben &amp; Jim went to Mr Bookers<span class='line-break'> </span> before breakfast Jim fed his<span class='line-break'> </span> stock and Ben milked his cows.<span class='line-break'> </span> Mr Booker &amp; family was at Mrs<span class='line-break'> </span> Jacksons. The cubian[?] went away<span class='line-break'> </span> this morning. Ernest &amp; Lottie Craddock<span class='line-break'> </span> and Johnson and Posie &amp; Bruce<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; his wife and Alice Thomson<span class='line-break'> </span> come to see Josie this<span class='line-break'> </span> morning. This evening Lee<span class='line-break'> </span> &amp; Grace Brumfield &amp; Carles <span class='line-break'> </span> and Virginia Harvey come<span class='line-break'> </span> to see her.  Well time is what<span class='line-break'> </span> I want. But I am glad that<span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas is over the excuse<span class='line-break'> </span> for idleness &amp; extravagance<span class='line-break'> </span> and I hope to see another<span class='line-break'> </span> Xmas but may not/amen</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2261">

<div class="page-content">
<p>366<span class='line-break'> </span> Memoranda<span class='line-break'> </span> The spotted cows calf came<span class='line-break'> </span> today, the 17th of August<span class='line-break'> </span> 1922.<span class='line-break'> </span> Peggies calf came the<span class='line-break'> </span> 11 of September 1922.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2262">
<h3><a name="page-2262">Memoranda (ii)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>367<span class='line-break'> </span> Memoranda<span class='line-break'> </span> Weighed five pounds<span class='line-break'> </span> of land that belonged to<span class='line-break'> </span> Jim. Sept the 12 1922<span class='line-break'> </span> 10 pounds</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-2263">
<h3><a name="page-2263">Memoranda (iii)</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>The first snow this year<span class='line-break'> </span> Jan the 14th 1922.<span class='line-break'> </span> One of the worst snows that I<span class='line-break'> </span> ever have seen fell today<span class='line-break'> </span> January the 27th 1922.<span class='line-break'> </span> Snow &amp; hail &amp; rain Feb the [?]<span class='line-break'> </span> Snowing this morning Feb the 7<span class='line-break'> </span> Snowed today Feb the 9th<span class='line-break'> </span> Snowed Feb the 15th &amp; 16th 1922<span class='line-break'> </span> March the 4th the tree was covered<span class='line-break'> </span> with ice this morning.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
</div>
